**This is the crux and the reason the issue was reopened twice.** The owner closed once on the `device_resident_inner_1017` fixture (`1.50 s`, converges in 1 iter) and **reopened**: that fixture is *not* the production path. The reproducible harness `examples/full_color_fit_1017.rs` then measured the **real** `run_joint_fit_arrow_schur` color-arm fit (n=180, output p=5120, but the decoder-β **border is k=15360**) and found: CPU assembly re-run **every** inner iteration (~1.4–2 s, 0 GPU), and one production InexactPCG solve **>45 s even capped at 2 iters** (a large fixed per-solve overhead, not iteration count). k=15360 > `DIRECT_SOLVE_MAX_K=2000` forces InexactPCG, and the resident `device_fit` frame has **no production caller** for that mode. The single-step resident routing (#2192) since removed the per-iterate re-upload on the *gradient* path, but device-resident **assembly** and a resident matrix-free PCG reused across the full outer loop — the rest of Phase 3 on the production color path — are still not benchmarked against the gate.

### Related-issue map (where residual work lives)
- CLOSED and folded: **#1551** (engagement/NVRTC), **#1412** (throughput), **#1014** (mixed-precision, Phase 2), **#1995** (moderate-K compute-bound), **#1082**.
- OPEN and carrying pieces: **#1026** (large-K reconstruction parity — the scientific payoff, held until the on-device large-K ladder is bit-correct), **#1033** (n-independent outer loop / resident reduced-Schur reuse), **#2227** (scale_k GPU sparse_dict hang at K=1e4).

### Verdict: **KEEP OPEN**
The engine substrate (engagement, residency, framed kernel, single-step resident routing) is landed and kernel-parity-validated on V100 — real, load-bearing progress. But the issue's **defining acceptance gates are wall-clock numbers on the full production fit** (color-arm ≤ 1.56 s, 8-layer ladder ≤ 2 min on A100), and those are **unmeasured**; the last production-path measurement was still ~26-min-class. The owner already made — and explicitly reverted — the "close on engagement/correctness alone" call, so closing now would repeat that error.

**What's left, precisely:**
1. A sanctioned **A100** benchmark of the full production color-arm fit (`examples/full_color_fit_1017.rs`) and the 8-layer transport ladder against the gates.
2. Device-resident **assembly** on the production color path (currently ~1.4–2 s CPU/inner-iter) + resident matrix-free PCG reused across the outer loop — the remaining Phase-3-on-production piece.
3. The **border-factoring lever** (shrink/factor the dense K×K H_bb border so n-row GPU-favorable work dominates; the full Newton is ~0.94× on GPU today) — informed by (1), unbenchmarked.
4. Phase 4 stream multiplexing — additive, separable.

Close only when (1) records the two wall-clock gates green on A100. (Recent incremental progress toward this: today's startup-tax host-budget gate before the CUDA probe, tagged "#1017 ordering"; the #2192 resident single-step routing.)

--- Comment 42/52 by @SauersML (2026-07-10T14:51:48Z) ---
## Production InexactPCG residency lifetime bug fixed (`022978df7`)

Current-HEAD audit found a concrete remaining production mismatch: `build_resident_sae_frame_if_admitted` admitted only `ArrowSolverMode::Direct`, but the full color-arm border is above `DIRECT_SOLVE_MAX_K` and therefore selects `InexactPCG`. The native InexactPCG device branch then called `solve_sae_matrix_free_pcg` directly on every LM ridge trial, re-flattening and re-uploading all ridge-independent SAE operands each retry. In other words, the resident frame existed but the actual large-border production mode was excluded from its lifetime.

`022978df7` makes the SAE resident frame ladder-scoped for both `Direct` and `InexactPCG`, and the native InexactPCG branch now resolves through `options.sae_resident_frame`. Only ridge-dependent `ainv` is refreshed per trial; `Unavailable` falls back to the established per-trial path, while numerical failures retain the existing fail-loud LM classification.

This is a real production-path residency increment, not a closure claim. GPU parity plus operand-byte/timing confirmation on the full color harness is still pending, and across-inner-iteration device assembly remains separate work.

--- Comment 43/52 by @SauersML (2026-07-10T15:04:18Z) ---
### Acceptance-harness defect found: reported EV came from the untouched seed

The #1017 hill-climb harness was not measuring optimizer output: after running the counted objective, it computed explained variance from `fixture.term` (the pristine seeded term) instead of consuming `counted.inner.into_fitted()`. Because the fixture target is constructed from that seed, the harness could report seed-perfect quality regardless of what the optimizer did.

The same harness also forced `OUTER_MAX_ITER=1` and used a wall-clock `--budget-ms` cliff. Per `SPEC.md`, those are being removed. The corrected acceptance path uses automatic Direct/InexactPCG routing, requires a genuinely converged fitted object, and computes quality from that returned fit. This is a harness correction, not yet a production performance claim.

--- Comment 44/52 by @SauersML (2026-07-10T15:07:08Z) ---
### Production color routing correction: current K=1 fixture is frame-reduced to Direct

A source-level audit found the old color harness was stale in a second way. Its full decoder coefficient width is `3 × 5120 = 15360`, but the joint fit calls `ensure_decoder_frames_active_for_current_decoder` before assembly. A `3 × 5120` decoder has numerical rank at most 3, so the exact Grassmann factorization reduces the assembled Newton border to at most `3 × 3 = 9`. Automatic routing therefore selects `Direct`, not `InexactPCG`, for this present K=1 color shape.

The InexactPCG resident-frame fix remains necessary for genuinely large *factored* borders, and commit `18ea4fe36` adds an LM-retry recording-frame regression for that path. The rewritten color harness now reports full beta width, assembled/factored width, and actual selected mode after requiring a converged REML fit; it no longer claims that this specific frame-reduced fixture exercises InexactPCG.

The device-resident inner-fit harness also swallowed solve failures: `time_fit` returned `Option`, all callers used `.ok()`, and repeated measurements retained a previous warm result if a later run errored. It printed convergence/parity booleans but still exited successfully.

The harness now propagates every `Result`, requires all CPU/device paths to converge, and asserts CPU/device parity. This prevents an A100 run with a failed or stale device solve from being reported as successful evidence.

--- Comment 47/52 by @SauersML (2026-07-10T19:56:25Z) ---
## SAE joint fit "0% GPU" profiled on an H100 — the dominant cost is a CPU threadpool-oversubscription bug, not (for this shape) a routing gap

Reproducing the #2015 full-scale behavior fit on an H100 (`sae_behavior_fit`, gamfit 0.1.253: activation 4000×256 PCA + behavior 4000×64, K=8 atoms, order-3 charts, outer REML): **0% GPU** (only a 520 MB CUDA context), and the CPU side runs at ~half efficiency.

### Profile (perf, single fixed-ρ inner fit, isolated)
- **~30% `spindle::Barrier::wait_and_clear_while`** — faer's threadpool barrier SPIN
- **~19–20% `__pv_queued_spin_lock_slowpath`** (+ overlapping futex_wait) — kernel contention from the same
- **~13% `spindle::worker_loop`**
- real compute: ~15% `assemble_arrow_schur_inner`, ~11% `CpuBatchedBlockSolver::block_gemm_subtract`

→ **~50–60% of all cycles are pure threadpool synchronization overhead.** (The original 4000×256 run: 34% barrier + 16.5% spinlock.)

### Root cause
`spindle` is **faer 0.24's internal threadpool.** faer's global parallelism defaults to `Par::rayon(0)` (faer/src/lib.rs:1112), and its high-level solvers (per-row Cholesky/eigendecomposition, the border factorization; `triangular_inverse` even hardcodes `Par::rayon(0)`) read `faer::get_global_parallelism()` directly. gam's SAE inner fit **already** fans the per-row assembly / factorization / reduced-Schur reduction across the global Rayon pool (`into_par_iter` over the n rows). Every faer solver reached inside those workers re-fans faer's spindle barrier pool **into the already-saturated outer fan-out** → nested oversubscription; the spindle workers busy-spin at the barrier. The existing `with_nested_parallel` guard (#1557) only pins gam's **own** `matmul` wrapper via `effective_global_parallelism`; it cannot reach faer's solvers (they take no parallelism argument — documented in faer_ndarray.rs:78-98).

### Why 0% GPU here
The 520 MB context is opened by `try_factor_blocks_batched` probing the device for the batched per-row Cholesky (factorization.rs:84) — a tiny fraction of the work. The dominant cost (per-row assembly + reduced-Schur reduction on `CpuBatchedBlockSolver`) is CPU-only. For K=8 (tiny per-row d×d blocks) the GPU is not the lever; the real defect is the CPU threadpool overhead. No silent NVRTC fallback was observed.

**Remaining GPU routing gap (for large-border shapes, not addressed here):** `CpuBatchedBlockSolver` is hardcoded at every arrow-schur call site — there is no `GpuBatchedBlockSolver` — and the framed matrix-free reduced-Schur build (`penalty_op` set by decoder frames) is excluded from `try_device_arrow_direct`, while `maybe_inject_gpu_schur_matvec` only fires in `InexactPCG` mode (the SAE inner solve runs Direct-mode dense reduced-Schur). So the reduced-Schur reduction has no device lane even where the border (Σ M_k·r_k) is large enough to win. That is the follow-up for the "device-resident SAE joint fit" goal.

### Fix
Hold a `FaerSequentialScope` (already in-tree, built for the #2074 topology-race deadlock but previously used only in `topology_selector`) across the fit so faer's solvers run single-threaded, while gam's coarse per-row Rayon parallelism (the real speedup) is untouched. Two commits:
- inner Newton fit (`run_joint_fit_arrow_schur`) — but that alone leaves the reduced-Schur **log-det** (run after it returns, in the REML criterion) on `Par::rayon(0)`, and the barrier-spin persisted (~29%).
- **whole `run_sae_crosscoder_fit`** — covers outer search / fixed-ρ solve, every inner fit, the log-det, and materialization.

faer reductions are parallelism-invariant (`Par::Seq` == `Par::rayon` bit-for-bit, `tests_parallelism_invariance_1557`), so **no fitted value changes** (R² identical before/after).

### Measured (H100, n=2000, p=128, K=8, isolated perf)
| | BEFORE (unpatched) | AFTER (whole-fit fix) |
|---|---|---|
| `spindle::Barrier::wait_and_clear_while` | ~30% | **0%** (gone) |
| `__pv_queued_spin_lock_slowpath` | ~19% | **0.14%** |
| `spindle::worker_loop` | ~13% | **0%** (gone) |
| top real-compute frames | 15% assemble + 11% block_gemm_subtract | 28% block_gemm_subtract + 21% FrameProjection::accumulate_output_project + 8% assemble |

**~50–63% of cycles were pure threadpool synchronization; the fix removes essentially all of it**, so the same wall-clock now does real arithmetic. The inner-fit-only scope alone did NOT clear it (~29% barrier persisted — the log-det pass runs outside `run_joint_fit`), which is why the scope had to cover the whole fit. `max_iter` does not bound the wall here (the log-det/refinement convergence dominates), so a single fit is minutes regardless — the barrier fraction is the reliable, contention-independent metric.

_R² identical before/after (parallelism-invariant), confirming no numerical change._


--- Comment 48/52 by @SauersML (2026-07-10T21:09:04Z) ---
# Design: full device residency of the inner SAE Newton fit (#1017)

Follow-up to the profiling comment above. The user's framing is correct — nothing in the math forbids running the whole inner Newton iteration on the GPU. This is the architecture for getting there, an honest inventory of what exists vs. what needs new kernels, a staged landing order with a measurable win per stage, and the **honest achievable speedup** (not 10,000×; see §4).

## 1. What the inner loop actually does (the residency target)

One inner Newton iteration of `run_joint_fit_arrow_schur`, per the code + profile:

| step | operation | today | cost class |
|---|---|---|---|
| A | **decode** `X̂_i = Σ_k a_ik·D_k(t_ik)` (atom basis eval + decoder) | rayon-CPU per row (`fill_decoded_row`) | O(n·K·M·p) |
| B | residual `e_i = X_i − X̂_i`, weighted metric | rayon-CPU | O(n·p) |
| C | **per-row Jacobian + Gauss–Newton blocks** `J_i`, `H_tt^(i)=JᵀJ`, `g_t^(i)`, `H_tβ^(i)`, frame projection | rayon-CPU (`assemble_arrow_schur_inner`, `FrameProjection::accumulate_output_project`) — **21%+8%+ of the fit; the big missing kernel** | O(n·d·k·…) |
| D | **batched factor** `chol(H_tt^(i)+ρ_t I)` | **device exists** (`try_factor_blocks_batched`→`try_cholesky_batched_lower_inplace`) | O(n·d³) |
| E | **reduced-Schur reduce** `S = H_ββ+ρ_β I − Σ_i H_βt^(i)(H_tt^(i))⁻¹H_tβ^(i)` | **device exists** (`tile_schur_partial`→`try_fast_atb_on_ordinal`), now single-GPU too (529c725d6); the 28% `block_gemm_subtract` | O(n·d·k²) |
| F | border factor `chol(S)` (k×k), solve `Δβ`, back-sub `Δt` | CPU (faer); dense-Direct device resident exists for the **non-framed** path (`ResidentArrowFrame`) | O(k³)+O(n·d·k) |
| G | **step + line search**: apply `(Δt,Δβ)`, re-evaluate objective (=A+B+loss) at trial steps | rayon-CPU | O(iters·n·K·M·p) |
| H | **softmax/logit** assignment update `a_ik = softmax(logits)_ik` | rayon-CPU | O(n·K) |

Residency dies today because **every iteration round-trips through the host**: the assembly (C) produces the per-row blocks on the CPU, D/E consume them (uploading per call), F comes back to the host, G/H run on the CPU. The buffers that are invariant across the whole inner walk — activation `X` (n×p), decoder coeffs (K×M×p), and the slowly-moving `coords t`/`logits` — are re-marshalled every step. That per-iteration H2D/D2H staging is the same tax #1412 measured (tile-GEMM stuck at 19% util because it re-uploaded `X` every call).

**Full residency = keep `X`, decoder, `coords`, `logits`, `assignments` in device buffers for the whole inner walk; only the outer-loop scalars (ρ, the accept/reject decision, the convergence norm) cross the bus.**

## 2. Inventory — exists vs. new kernels

**Exists and reusable (compose, do not duplicate):**
- `try_cholesky_batched_lower_inplace` — batched per-row Cholesky (step D).
- `try_fast_atb_on_ordinal` — the stacked `(Σd×k)ᵀ(Σd×k)` reduce GEMM (step E), now reachable single-GPU.
- `ResidentArrowFrame` / `ResidentBaseArrowFrameHandle` (gpu_kernels/arrow_schur.rs) — device-resident batched POTRF/TRSM/Schur/border for the **dense Direct** path; the residency skeleton stages A–F once and refactors per ridge. **Disqualified today only because it reads dense `hbb` and the framed path sets a `penalty_op`.**
- `DeviceSaePcgData` + the `PCG_VECTOR` NVRTC kernels (#1551) — the framed matrix-free **step** solve on device (step F for framed).
- cuSOLVER `Dpotrf`/`Dtrsm`, NVRTC infra (`device_cache::compile_ptx_arch`, arch-pinned per #1551).

**New kernels required (the actual work):**
1. **Device decode (A) + loss (B/G):** evaluate each atom's basis at `t_ik`, GEMV against decoder coeffs, accumulate `Σ_k a_ik·(·)`, form residual and the scalar objective. Reused verbatim for the line-search trials.
2. **Device Jacobian + GN-block assembly (C):** the big one — per-row basis-Jacobian, frame `Uᵀ` projection, and the `JᵀJ / Jᵀe / H_tβ` reductions, written straight into the resident slab that D/E consume. This is what makes A→E a single resident chain with no host copy.
3. **Device softmax/logit update (H).**
4. **Device step application (part of G):** in-place `t += αΔt`, `β += αΔβ` on resident buffers.

## 3. Staged landing order (measurable win per stage)

- **Stage 0 (baseline, DONE):** faer-Seq barrier fix + single-GPU reduce GEMM (529c725d6). Measurement in the next comment.
- **Stage 1 (biggest single win): resident A→C→D→E chain.** New device assembly kernel (#2 above) writes the per-row blocks directly to device memory that the existing batched Cholesky (D) and stacked-GEMM reduce (E) consume — no host copy between assembly, factor, and reduce. Moves ~50–60% of inner-loop compute (C is 30%+, E is 28%). Parity-gated (device dense reduced-Schur == CPU to fp tol). Crossover: engage at the same work floor as E (K≥64 / large border); small K stays CPU.
- **Stage 2: resident border solve + step (F,G-apply).** Extend `ResidentArrowFrame` to accept the framed operators (or add a framed sibling) so `Δβ`/`Δt` are produced and applied on device; `coords`/`decoder` buffers become persistent across iterations. Removes the per-iteration step round-trip.
- **Stage 3: resident line-search objective (G).** Device decode+loss (#1) evaluated at trial α without leaving the device — only the scalar objective crosses. Kills the O(iters·n·K·M·p) host decode.
- **Stage 4: resident softmax (H) + full loop.** Whole inner iteration resident; only ρ, accept/reject, and the convergence scalar cross per outer step.

Each stage is independently parity-gated and measured; the fit stays correct (CPU-identical to fp tolerance) at every stage.

## 4. Honest speedup accounting (not 10,000×)

The inner loop is ~99% of the fit wall (the outer ρ walk is a handful of inner fits). Its device-able fraction (A–H) is ~95%+ — everything is per-row-batched or a dense k×k solve. So Amdahl's serial residue is small; the ceiling is set by **how fast the device-able work actually runs**, and that is where 10,000× breaks:

- **10,000× is the raw f64 FLOP ratio on one peak GEMM**, not an end-to-end number. An H100 does ~30–60 TFLOP/s f64 vs ~0.2–0.5 TFLOP/s effective on ~10 CPU cores — a ~60–150× hardware ratio, and only the large stacked GEMM (step E at K≥256) approaches it.
- The rest of the loop is **many small batched ops** (per-row d×d Cholesky, d×k Jacobians, K-wide softmax) that do not saturate an H100 — realistically 5–30× each.
- **f64** halves/quarters tensor throughput; small-batch launch overhead and the k×k border Cholesky (serial-ish) cap it further.

**Honest end-to-end ceiling: ~10–50× wall at large K/border (K≥64, wide border), 60–90% util once resident** — with the biggest lever being residency itself (eliminating the #1412 staging tax), not raw FLOPs. To push toward ~100× you need the *whole* loop resident (stages 1–4) *and* shapes large enough to saturate (K≥256, n≥16K). A single-op microbench (step E alone at K=256, resident) can show ~100–150× and I'll report it as the FLOP-ceiling proof point, but the fit-level number will be tens of ×, and I'd rather promise that and beat it than quote 10,000×.

Concretely: stage 1 alone should take the large-K inner fit from CPU-bound to ~5–15× with 40–70% util; stages 2–4 compound toward the tens-of-× ceiling.

Stage-0 baseline numbers (H100, K=64, CPU-reduction vs device-reduction) follow in the next comment; stage-1 assembly kernel lands after.

## Stage-0 measurement + Stage-1 prerequisites (#1017)

### Stage-0 numbers (H100, n=2000, PCA=256, K=64, 3 inner iters)

Baseline = faer-fix wheel (CPU reduce); Device = + the single-GPU reduced-Schur GEMM (529c725d6). Same fit, GPU sampled once/sec during the run.

| | GPU util (peak) | GPU mem | reduction path |
|---|---|---|---|
| baseline (CPU reduce) | **0%** | 1055 MiB | rayon CPU fold |
| device (reduce GEMM) | **~1%** | **1580 MiB** (+525) | `try_fast_atb_on_ordinal` cuBLAS |

**Honest read:** the device reduction **does engage** — GPU memory rises by ~525 MiB on the device arm (the stacked `(Σd×k)ᵀ(Σd×k)` operands + cuBLAS workspace), which is absent on the CPU baseline. But **end-to-end GPU util stays ~1%**, because at this shape the O(n·d·k²) reduction is a sub-millisecond blip in a fit that is still dominated by the **CPU per-row assembly** (the ~30% Jacobian / GN-block / frame-projection work that runs on rayon). The device spends ~99% of the fit idle, waiting on CPU assembly.

This is exactly the thesis of the design comment above: **stage-0 correctly offloads the reduction, but it cannot move utilization on its own** — the assembly is the gate. Real GPU util requires stage 1 (device-resident assembly) so the device isn't starved. Stage-0's reduce-GEMM only becomes a wall win when the border is large enough that the reduction dominates (K≥256, wide border) **and** the assembly feeding it is also resident. So: stage-0 is a correct, parity-safe increment and a necessary piece, but the measured lesson is that **the assembly kernel (stage 1) is the real unlock** — no partial-offload shortcut moves the needle.

### Stage-1 prerequisites (for the next sanctioned GPU session — start cold in minutes)

**Environment:** a dedicated GPU box with an **exclusive warm cargo target**. The blocker this session was shared-target lock contention (20–30 min *blocked* builds behind other lanes) — fatal to NVRTC build→test→debug cycles, which need to be minutes each.

**Entry point (where the kernel installs):** `SaeManifoldTerm::assemble_arrow_schur_inner` in `crates/gam-sae/src/manifold/construction_arrow_schur_assembly.rs` — specifically the per-row `into_par_iter().map_init(...)` closure (~line 935) that today runs `with_nested_parallel(|| … )` on rayon. The device kernel replaces the per-row body: decode (`atom.fill_decoded_row`) → residual → basis-Jacobian → frame projection (`FrameProjection::accumulate_output_project`) → GN blocks (`H_tt^(i)`, `g_t^(i)`, `H_tβ^(i)`), writing the `ArrowRowBlock` slab **directly to device memory** that `try_factor_blocks_batched` (factor) and `tile_schur_partial`→`try_fast_atb_on_ordinal` (reduce) then consume with no host copy. Coords/decoder/activation buffers stay resident across iterations.

**Parity gate:** device-assembled `(H_tt^(i), g_t^(i), H_tβ^(i))` and the resulting dense reduced Schur must equal the `CpuBatchedBlockSolver` path to ≤1e-9 relative, on the `dense_direct_system` fixture + a real qwen/OLMo shape. Reuse the structure of `parallel_dense_schur_reduction_deterministic_and_matches_sequential` (arrow_schur/tests.rs:2987).

**NVRTC discipline (per #1551 / the nvrtc-silent-CPU sweep):** arch-pinned `device_cache::compile_ptx_arch`; standalone-compile the kernel source with libnvrtc on a login node FIRST (the cheap faithful oracle); **fail loud** on compile/launch error — never silent-CPU-fallback (that's how a "device" path becomes a phantom).

**Routing:** same measured crossover as stage-0 (engage when `assembly_work ≥ gemm_min_flops`); small K stays CPU. No flags.

**Realistic target:** stage-1 (resident assembly→factor→reduce) should take the large-K inner fit to ~5–15× with 40–70% util; stages 2–4 (border solve, line-search objective, softmax resident) compound toward the ~10–50× fit-level ceiling from the design comment. Not 10,000×.


--- Comment 50/52 by @SauersML (2026-07-10T22:56:04Z) ---
## CPU hot-path follow-up to the oversubscription fix: the two top profile items, landed

The post-`FaerSequentialScope` profile of the joint SAE fit was dominated by `block_gemm_subtract` (~28%) and `FrameProjection::accumulate_output_project` (~21%). Both are now restructured on main (swept into `b21f389cd`):

**1. Chunk-stacked reduced-Schur subtraction** (`gam-solve/src/arrow_schur/system.rs`, `ChunkSchurStack`). The parallel assembly's per-row `d×k²` scalar scatter against a randomly indexed `k×k` accumulator becomes ONE sequential SIMD GEMM per 64-row chunk (`s_part −= LᵀR` via faer, `Par::Seq` inside the worker per #1557) — the CPU mirror of the device `tile_schur_partial` stacking. Sparse top-k rows keep the nnz-scaled scatter (#1995) via a derived crossover: scatter costs `Σ_c nnz_l·nnz_r` unvectorizable FMAs vs the row's `d·k²/8` share of the GEMM at ≈8 f64 FMAs/cycle, so the GEMM wins above `scatter_flops > d·k²/8`; the pricing scan is the same `O(d·k)` pass the scatter already pays.

**2. Frame-projection hoist** (`gam-sae/frames.rs::project_jacobian_rows` + the assembly caller). The projection `J_row·U_k` is basis-column independent, but the assembly re-derived it `m` times per (row, atom) through per-scalar `accumulate_output_project` calls — `m·q·p` calls each doing a rank-length axpy. Now ONE `q×p · p×r` GEMM per (row, atom) + rank-length axpys per basis column: ~`m×` flop reduction on framed fits (m = basis size, typically 7–13). Unframed atoms take a bit-identical raw-row axpy.

**Verified** (both changes, local battery): `parallel_streaming_assembly_deterministic_and_matches_sequential`, `parallel_schur_matvec_deterministic_and_matches_sequential`, `block_gemm_subtract_matches_dense_on_sparse_column_support` — 3/3 PASS. The contract preserved is exactly the documented one: bit-identical run-to-run, tolerance-equal to the serial fold (the stacked GEMM is the same reassociation class as the existing chunk-partial fold and the device stacking).

Wall-clock A/B (600-row real behavior gate + synthetic crosscoder battery, HEAD vs `32b2fb34d`) is running on MSI (job 12962745, 32-core warm target); numbers will follow in this thread. Note the gate itself currently fails by convergence refusal (#2015 crawl — separate fix in progress), so the timing compares equal-iteration-budget walls.

Closing the loop on why the GPU program kept finding an idle device: the binding constraint was iteration count × pipeline depth, not FLOPs — at measured inner contraction ~0.998/iter, the criterion evaluation spent its life in O(n·q·k²) assembly for steps that closed 0.2% of the gap each, and the default pipeline multiplied that through race × whitening passes × probes (#2267). ================================================================================
ISSUE #2015: Behavior-anchored joint atoms: shared-latent two-block fit (activation + Hellinger behavior block), coupling weight by REML — nats-calibrated coordinates, measured isometry defect, behavior-pinned gauge
================================================================================
Author: SauersML
Created: 2026-07-01T22:40:46Z
URL: https://github.com/SauersML/gam/issues/2015
Comments: 14
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
BODY:
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
## Idea
For tokens with a behavioral readout $p_i$ (concept-restricted next-token distribution with an 'other' bin — the manifold-steering paper's construction — or a probe head), fit the dictionary **jointly** over two response blocks with a **shared** per-token latent $t_{ik}$ and shared gates:

- activation block: $h_i \approx \sum_k a_{ik}\,\Phi_k(t_{ik})B_k$
- behavior block: $\sqrt{p_i} \approx \exp_{b_*}\big(\sum_k a_{ik}\,\Psi_k(t_{ik})C_k\big)$ (tangent-space fit at a Fréchet mean, decoded through the sphere exp-map — `manifold_exp_map`/`manifold_log_map` FFI already exist)

with the cross-block coupling weight $\lambda_y$ selected by REML like any smoothing parameter.

## Why this is more than a feature
1. **Isometry as inductive bias with a dial, not an assumption.** The steering paper's headline finding is that activation and behavior manifolds are (scaled-)isometric on natural data. Here $\lambda_y$ and the per-atom cross-block residual are *estimated*, so 'representation–behavior isometry defect' becomes a reported per-atom statistic. Atoms where the correspondence fails are flagged instead of silently distorted.
2. **Chart semantics and gauge pinning for free.** The steering paper concedes its intrinsic coordinates are supervised (ground-truth ordinals / atan2 on 2 PCs). Here $t$ is defined by what it does to behavior. Concretely: gauge generators the activation block leaves flat (chart origin, orientation/reflection) are pinned by the behavior block — directly measurable with the RRQR identifiability certificate as converted free→pinned generators. (Caveat: that certificate currently misbehaves, #1880 — fixing it is a soft prerequisite for *measuring* the pinning, not for the fit.)
3. **Universal physical units.** Put the unit-speed gauge on the *behavior* block. With $q=\sqrt p$: $ds^2_{\mathrm{FR}}=\sum dp_i^2/p_i = 4\|dq\|^2$ and $\mathrm{KL}(p\|p+dp)\approx \tfrac12 ds^2_{\mathrm{FR}}$, so a unit-speed chart in $q$-space satisfies $\mathrm{KL}(t\to t+\delta) = 2\delta^2 + O(\delta^3)$ — identically for every atom, task, layer, model. One chart unit = fixed nats. `steer_delta`'s `predicted_nats` becomes calibrated by construction, and transfer-operator entries (see the chart-calculus issue) become cross-model commensurable.

## Relation to #980 (completed)
#980 landed Fisher-weighted *reconstruction* (`fisher_factors` shard, `RowMetric::OutputFisher`, rho_cascade refinement). This proposal is the successor, not a duplicate: instead of reweighting activation errors by behavioral sensitivity, the behavior is reconstructed *as a response block* with a shared coordinate — which is what yields gauge pinning, a defect statistic, and the universal calibration. The staged `fisher_factors` harvest is reusable for building the y-block.

## Implementation locality
gam already fits tangent-space sphere-valued responses and multi-block designs with per-block REML weights; the shared latent adds rows to the same per-token arrow block. The unit-speed re-gauge is a post-fit reparameterization exactly like the #1019 arc-length canonicalization, just computed on the y-block chart image.

## Acceptance
On the steering paper's four Llama-3.1-8B L28 tasks (harvest via `gamfit/torch/harvest.py`): (a) unsupervised joint fit recovers their supervised spline chart under their own isometry protocol; (b) measured nats per unit $t$ along natural arcs ≈ 2 (the kill test already noted on #1942); (c) identifiability report shows origin/orientation generators pinned by the y-block that are free in an activation-only fit.

## Non-goals
No new atom types; no Fisher sketch changes; `softmax_topk`-style torch-only lanes unaffected.

--- Comment 1/14 by @SauersML (2026-07-01T22:56:44Z) ---
Sequencing note after the whitened-likelihood finding (#2021): the RowMetric seam that #2021 exercises is the same seam this issue's behavior block enters through — today `row_metric_from_fisher_provenance` installs a gauge metric at `latent_basis_and_sae_ffi.rs:2664`; the upgrade path is metric → second weighted response block (√p in the tangent plane) with shared t and REML-selected λ_y. So the dependency order is #2021 + #2022 first, then this — and nothing built there is throwaway: it is one weighted-likelihood seam carrying three payloads in sequence (interference whitening → Fisher weighting → behavior anchoring). Attempting the joint two-block fit on the current iid likelihood would stack a second response block on a foundation whose dispersion is already mis-estimated (#1892 mechanism), so the isometry-defect statistic this issue promises would be confounded by the very over-smoothing #2021 removes.

--- Comment 2/14 by @SauersML (2026-07-08T02:16:59Z) ---
## Increment landed: the per-atom representation–behavior **isometry defect** (point 1's reported statistic)

### Inventory first — what already exists

The **core** of this issue (shared-latent two-block fit with REML-weighted coupling, λ_y a variance component not a knob) is **already landed**, in the manifold lane rather than the sparse_dict lane:

- `crates/gam-sae/src/manifold/behavior.rs` — `SphereTangentEmbedding` (√p half-density map, √2 nats scaling, exact decode round-trip, `predicted_nats`/`exact_kl`/`fisher_rao_distance`) and `BehaviorBlock` (augmented target `Z̃ = [Z | √λ_y·Y]`, `split_decoder`, closed-form REML variance-ratio update `reml_updated_log_lambda_y = (R_x/p_x)/(R_y/p_y)` + its `√λ_y` change-of-variables Jacobian). Generalised to K blocks by `OutputBlock` + `stack_augmented_target`.
- `crates/gam-sae/src/manifold/behavior_fit.rs` — `SaeManifoldTerm::run_two_block_reml_fit` / `run_multiblock_reml_fit`: the outer `(fit at λ, closed-form λ-update)` block-coordinate descent on the joint profiled criterion. **λ_y is selected by data, never a knob.**
- `crates/gam-sae/src/manifold/tests_behavior_twoblock_rung2.rs` already proves: joint reconstruction of both blocks under one shared `t`; `reml_selects_lambda_y_at_planted_variance_ratio` (starting-point-invariant, lands on σ_x²/σ_y²); and the flagship `behavior_block_pins_reflection_gauge_that_activation_alone_cannot` — the activation image is reflection-symmetric so an activation-only fit *provably* collapses mirror pairs, and the behavior block pins the reflection (per-row KL < 0.1× the planted mirror separation).

### On reusing `cofit.rs` (f0f69d9ff)

Evaluated. `sparse_dict/cofit.rs` is a genuine two-block, one-objective, **monotone alternation** — the same *shape* — but it is the **wrong seam** for this issue: its two blocks are the *linear codes* vs the *curved charts*, **both reconstructing activations**, with no behavior target and objective `‖x − L − C‖²_F + λ_lin‖codes‖²_F`. The behavior-anchored joint fit's two blocks are *activation* vs *behavior* (`behavior_fit.rs`), which already implements the same alternation-on-one-penalised-objective pattern with the REML variance-ratio coupling. So the right move was **not** to build parallel plumbing in cofit.rs, nor to duplicate the two-block fit, but to add the one artifact this issue promises that was **not** yet reported.

### The gap this increment closes — point 1's "reported per-atom statistic"

> *"λ_y and the per-atom cross-block residual are estimated, so 'representation–behavior isometry defect' becomes a reported per-atom statistic. Atoms where the correspondence fails are flagged instead of silently distorted."*

That statistic did not exist. The within-chart `atom_coordinate_fidelity` (#2081) is purely activation-internal; nothing compared the **activation-induced** geometry to the **behavior-induced** geometry along the shared latent.

**Landed** (`crates/gam-sae/src/manifold/behavior_isometry.rs`, `atom_behavior_isometry` / `behavior_isometry_report`, commit `40fe6b859`):

For a fitted `d=1` two-block atom, split the augmented decoder into `B_k` (activation) and nats-unit `C_k` (behavior, `√λ_y` un-done via `BehaviorBlock::split_decoder`), evaluate the basis first-jet at the fitted rows (**reusing** `chart_canonicalization::curve_speeds`, now `pub(crate)`), and form the two induced speeds along the shared `t`:

```
s_x(t) = ‖Φ'(t) B_k‖ ,   s_y(t) = ‖Φ'(t) C_k‖ .
```

Scaled-isometry ⟺ `r(t) = s_x/s_y` constant. Reported per atom:
- **`scale`** = support-weighted mean of `r` (the paper's isometry scale),
- **`defect_cv`** = support-weighted CV of `r` — **0 ⟺ exact scaled isometry**, large ⟺ the correspondence bends (the flag),
- **`nats_per_unit_t`** = weighted mean of `s_y²` — the behavioral dose in nats per unit `t²` (`predicted_nats`), i.e. the calibration readout for point 3 / acceptance (b),
- `min/max_ratio_over_scale`, `behavior_engaged` (false ⟺ inert `C_k`, defect = NaN — no correspondence to certify, reported honestly rather than as a defect).

**Key property (why no chart canonicalization is needed):** the defect is a *ratio of two speeds w.r.t. the same t*, so under any reparameterization `t↦u(t)` both speeds pick up the same Jacobian and the ratio is invariant. **The defect is gauge-invariant** — it does not depend on the residual `Diff(S¹)` gauge the fit landed in. This is complementary to the arc-length defect (which asks "is the chart honest?"); this asks "does the honest chart carry the *same* geometry in activation and behavior?".

### Test — planted-truth, fails-before/passes-after (`tests_behavior_isometry_2015.rs`)

`isometry_defect_separates_isometric_from_broken`: **identical** activation circle in both arms (so no activation-only statistic can tell them apart), behavior traverses its circle at angular position `ψ(t)`:
- **isometric** `ψ = 2πt` (constant speed) → asserts `defect_cv < 0.15`,
- **broken** `ψ = 2πt + 0.8·sin 2πt` (`ψ'` sweeps 0.2·2π … 1.8·2π, ~9× range) → asserts `defect_cv > 0.30`, and `broken > 2×·isometric`.

Both run through the **real** `run_joint_fit_arrow_schur` two-block fit (EV>0.85 precondition on each block before reading speeds). Plus three deterministic unit tests on the estimator arithmetic: constant ratio → `scale=3.0`, `defect=0`; planted `r = 1+0.5cos` → `defect_cv ≈ 0.354` (= 0.5/√2, the exact CV); inert behavior → `behavior_engaged=false`, `defect=NaN`. (CI compiles/runs; my local box is saturated by concurrent gam-sae builds.)

### What remains (kept out of this increment, in dependency order)

1. **Acceptance (b) — pin `nats_per_unit_t → 2`.** Reported now; driving it to a constant is the behavior-block **arc-length re-gauge** (the #1019-style unit-speed reparam applied to the y-block chart image, exactly as point 3 describes). This module gives the measurement that re-gauge closes the loop on.
2. **Acceptance (c) — pinned generators.** Wire `defect_cv` and the behavior-pinned gauge generators into the identifiability certificate (`identifiability.rs`) as converted free→pinned generators; soft-blocked on the RRQR certificate #1880.

This is a genuine fork inside a hot, heavily-used pyfunction; the term-build + block-install + preconditions (each block EV, `behavior_engaged`) must be exercised on a real fit. --- Comment 4/14 by @SauersML (2026-07-08T16:30:32Z) ---
## #2015 correction — the behavior FFI is NOT a fork of `sae_manifold_fit`; it needs an augmented-width term (my earlier spec was wrong on this)

I started implementing (b) as the fork my previous comment described (optional `behavior_probs` on `sae_manifold_fit` → `set_behavior_block` → `run_two_block_reml_fit`) and hit a hard invariant that makes that path incorrect. Reverted; here is the corrected design so the next attempt lands in one MSI pass instead of discovering this at compile time.

### The blocker: `set_behavior_block` requires atoms built at the augmented width

`SaeManifoldTerm::set_behavior_block` (`construction.rs:1284`) enforces `block.augmented_dim() == self.output_dim()`, i.e. every atom's decoder must be `M × (p_x + p_y)` — the activation columns `[0,p_x)` plus the behavior tangent columns `[p_x, p_x+p_y)`. Confirmed by the passing test `tests_behavior_twoblock_rung2.rs:88-126`: it builds the atom at `p_tot = p_x + p_y` (`augmented_circle_atom(&evaluator, &coords, p_tot)`) *before* `set_behavior_block`, and `run_two_block_reml_fit(activation)` re-stacks `[Z | √λ_y·Y]` internally each sweep.

`sae_manifold_fit` builds its atoms at the **activation** width `p_x` (from the caller's `decoder_coefficients`, shape `(K,M,p_x)`), and its whole preamble — `seed_reconstruction_dispersion(z_view)`, shape-uncertainty bands, `p_out` — assumes `p_out = p_x`. So a fork that installs a behavior block on that term fails the `augmented_dim` check, and widening `p_out` to the augmented width to satisfy it breaks the activation-width preamble. The fork is structurally the wrong shape.

### Correct design: a standalone `sae_manifold_behavior_fit` pyfunction (augmented-width construction)

A separate pyfunction, sharing the atom-construction helpers but building at augmented width:

1. Take the same term-construction args as `sae_manifold_fit` (`z`, `atom_basis`, `atom_dim`, `basis_values`, `basis_jacobian`, `basis_sizes`, `decoder_coefficients`, `initial_logits`, `initial_coords`, `alpha`, `tau`, `assignment_kind`, the inner ridge/step knobs) **plus** `behavior_probs (n×V)` and `behavior_max_sweeps`.
2. `let block = BehaviorBlock::fit(behavior_probs, p_x, 0.0)?;  let p_y = block.behavior_dim();` (`= V−1`).
3. **Pad the decoders to augmented width:** reshape `decoder_coefficients` from `(K,M,p_x)` to `(K,M,p_x+p_y)`, zero-filling the behavior columns (the fit learns them, warm-started from the activation solution). This is the one new construction step.
4. Build evaluators (`build_sae_basis_evaluators`, unchanged — the basis is output-width-independent) and the term via `term_from_padded_blocks_with_mode` at `p_out = p_x + p_y` (imported from `ffi_prelude`).
5. `term.set_behavior_block(block)?;` (now the `augmented_dim` check passes) → `term.run_two_block_reml_fit(z_view /* p_x activation */, &mut init_rho, penalties, TwoBlockRemlControls{ max_sweeps: behavior_max_sweeps, inner_max_iter, step_size, ridge_ext_coord, ridge_beta, log_lambda_tol: 1e-4 })?`.
6. Return `{ log_lambda_y, sweeps, converged, lambda_identifiable, loss_data_fit, behavior_isometry: [ {atom_idx, behavior_engaged, scale, defect_cv, nats_per_unit_t, ...} ] }` from `behavior_isometry_report(&term)`.

This is ~100 lines mirroring the construction preamble (coord blocks, atom centers, basis kinds, mode, init_rho) — a real function, not a thin surface, and it must be exercised on a real two-block fit (the padding, the augmented `output_dim`, the per-block EV preconditions). It should go through the MSI loop, not land blind.

### Net

No code landed this pass — the fork I began was structurally wrong and reverted. The corrected finding: exposing behavior_probs means a standalone augmented-width fit pyfunction (decoder padding + `term_from_padded_blocks_with_mode` at `p_x+p_y`), not a param on `sae_manifold_fit`. The core (behavior.rs / behavior_fit.rs / behavior_isometry.rs) is untouched and still solid. (a) nats→2 regauge and (c) generator pinning are unchanged from the prior status. Still recommend NOT closing.


--- Comment 5/14 by @SauersML (2026-07-08T21:04:58Z) ---
Partial hardening landed in 7c95a0c31 (not a resolver for the behavior-block / measured-isometry-defect work here): the isometry penalty's **user-supplied reference metric is now scale-normalized**.

Before: `R_n = g_n/ḡ − g_ref_n` — the decoder metric was normalized by its own average trace `ḡ`, but the reference was subtracted raw, so a decoder metric exactly proportional to the supplied reference had a nonzero residual unless the reference already had avg-trace-per-dim = 1.

After: `R_n = g_n/ḡ − g_ref_n/ḡ_ref`, with `ḡ_ref = (1/Nd)·Σ tr(g_ref_n)` via a shared `average_trace_per_dim`. A proportional decoder metric now has zero residual. Euclidean reference preserved bit-for-bit (`ḡ_ref=1`); gradient/Hessian form unchanged (the offset is constant w.r.t. decoder coords).

--- Comment 10/14 by @SauersML (2026-07-10T21:24:29Z) ---
## #2015 inner-solve stall: root cause (measured), and why the obvious fix is wrong

Instrumented the deterministic 600-row gate (`qwen_real_activation_behavior_fit_selects_identifiable_lambda_y`) on real Qwen3.5-9B L21 data with per-iterate eprintln probes on the A10 box. The typed refusal is correct SPEC behavior; the defect is the stall, and it is **not** boundary-hook damage at this scale.

### What the failure actually is

Baseline runs refuse with a *relative* KKT gradient that plateaus around 0.3–0.5 (nowhere near the `1e-5` relative tolerance):

- `‖g‖=142.5`, tol `3.075e-3` (iterate-scale 307 → relative **0.46**), 660 inner iters (original report).
- `‖g‖=82.0`, tol `2.750e-3` (iterate-scale 275 → relative **0.30**), 630 inner iters (re-run).

Per-iterate trace: the penalized objective descends `3.11e7 → ~1.7e5` fast (99%+), then **crawls** — the inner arrow KKT residual falls ~1.7%/iterate (linear rate ≈ 0.983). Reaching the `1e-5` relative tolerance from a ~0.4 plateau at that rate needs thousands of iterations; the refine budget (~660) dies first.

### Mechanism (ill-conditioning + line-search overshoot, not hooks)

- The augmented two-block target is `n=600, p̃=127` (`p_x=64` activation PCA + `p_y=63` behavior sphere-tangent). Output column L2 norms span **1.3e4**: activation PC0 ≈ `11.55`, smallest column ≈ `8.9e-4` (the √λ_y-scaled behavior columns are the small end, ≈ `0.12` and below). Joint `(t,β)` Hessian condition number ≈ **1e8**.
- The fit routes onto Grassmann output frames by default at this width (`frames_active=true`).
- Each iterate the **pure Newton step is accepted** (`prox=false`), but `‖Δ‖≈12–20` while `‖g‖≈700–940` and `cos(g,Δ)=gᵀΔ/(‖g‖‖Δ‖)≈0.04`: the full step overshoots this nonlinear, ill-conditioned objective, so the Armijo line search backtracks to `step_size≈0.05` every iterate → linear crawl.
- Boundary hooks are benign here: post unit-speed-retraction objective == accepted; the frame re-polar **helps** early (`post_frame < obj`) and only mildly raises it late (`~+1e-4·obj`). So the H100 4000-row "boundary-hook damage / incumbent restore" is a *separate, larger-scale* regime, not the 600-row stall.

### a / b / c

Primarily **(a) + (c)**: a pre-existing ill-conditioning/globalization weakness of the joint Newton on wide targets, tipped past the budget by the **behavior augmentation's extra column-scale spread** (the tiny √λ_y sphere-tangent columns extend the ratio to ~1.3e4). **Not primarily (b)**: the deleted `optimize_log_amplitudes_closed_form`/`pin_scale_gauge` machinery used to mask this by closed-form-solving the decoder scale each accepted iterate; its removal is an *amplifier* of the crawl, not the root.

### Fix that was tried and REVERTED (so it is not re-attempted)

The #1026 closed-form decoder-LSQ polish — the natural decoder-scale rescue — is gated OFF whenever frames are active (`fit_drivers.rs`: `if max_iter > 0 && !self.frames_active()`), so the wide frame-active fit never gets it. Enabling it in the frame-active path (with an in-frame re-projection `B ← (B U) Uᵀ` to avoid desyncing the fixed frame `U`) **lowered the objective ~40%** (`data_fit 1.45e5 → 9.4e4`) but moved the state **away** from joint-KKT stationarity (relative KKT gradient `0.46 → 5.7`) and made the gate fail *faster*. A block-coordinate decoder optimum is not a joint-Newton stationary point, and `reml_criterion` gates acceptance on the joint KKT gradient — so this improves model quality but cannot satisfy the convergence gate. Reverted.

### Recommended fix (solver-level)

Column-equilibrate the augmented target for the inner solve: `D = diag(‖col‖)`, fit against `Z̃ D⁻¹`, fold `D` back into the decoder (`B_true = B_w D`). Every output column then contributes at unit curvature to the shared coordinate, so the globalized Newton takes full steps and converges quadratically instead of crawling. Equivalent principled route: a variable-projection (Golub–Pereyra) reformulation that eliminates the linear decoder `β` and runs Newton on the coordinate `t` alone (well-conditioned). Either is a substantial change spanning the decoder representation, penalties, and the evidence log-det, and must land with its ρ/θ-adjoint to avoid the classic obj↔grad desync.

## Fleet-wide fit regression found by bisect and FIXED — unblocks this issue's gates and the #2240 zoo

An independent full gam-sae suite run on MSI (job 12960183) showed **1072 passed / 126 FAILED** — broad real-fit reds (this issue's 600-row gate, the OLMo crosscoder gate, zoo fits, planted-circle seeds, "no candidate seeds passed outer startup validation").

**Bisect** (MSI job 12962841, oracle = `olmo_l18_l19_pair_crosscoder_fits_with_measured_drift`): first bad commit = `6297a7e9f` — the morning ban-scanner unblock. Its "assignment: rho params now enforce a rho↔dictionary shape contract" invented a validation rejecting any ρ whose per-atom width ≠ `k_atoms()`. But K legitimately moves mid-fit (births, deaths, compaction, topology-race candidates) while ρ updates lag — the contract vetoed valid states and broke seed validation and real fits fleet-wide.

**Fix (pushed):** the contract is deleted, and the original scanner complaint (an unused `_rho` param) is resolved honestly — the row gates are ρ-invariant post-#1033, so the assignment APIs now take **no ρ at all**; the vestigial ρ threading was removed through the entire caller cascade (assignments, amplitudes, encoder fitting, frame refresh, seeding, jet window, block IFT RHS). The invariance is now structural (stated by the signatures), and the old ρ-invariance test becomes a purity check.

Consequences: the crawl diagnosis on this issue stands (high-residual Gauss-Newton direction failure — LM-damping fix in progress), but every measurement taken on post-6297a/pre-fix builds is contaminated by the seed-validation regression and should be re-run — including the #2240 zoo walls and the #2022 A/B.

--- Comment 13/14 by @SauersML (2026-07-11T16:01:14Z) ---
## Status 2026-07-11: acceptance gate is red on the shared inner-solve wall, not a behavior-block defect

The #2015 acceptance test `qwen_real_activation_behavior_fit_selects_identifiable_lambda_y` (600 real Qwen-3.5-9B L21 PCA-64 rows) currently fails — but the failure is **not** in the behavior-anchored two-block design; it's the shared SAE inner-solve convergence wall tracked in #2228.

Log-confirmed (GHA validate-one run `29144079962`, real `running 1 test`, 2624s):
```
inner solve did not converge at fixed ρ; ‖g‖=1.410137 nor ‖Π⊥gauge g‖=1.387610
met tolerance 2.760312e-3 after 1050 inner iterations
```
The current fix cluster (LM + one-referee guard + structured-residual floor) already took this from ‖g‖=241 (a misleading near-exact 48-row regime) to 1.41 (correct high-residual regime) — ~170× — but an O(1) residual floor remains. Full data + the decisive inner-budget-trajectory experiment are in **#2228** (the canonical home of this wall). #2015 unblocks when that certifies. Behavior-block machinery (Hellinger block, λ_y selection) is not implicated by this failure.


--- Comment 14/14 by @SauersML (2026-07-11T18:25:45Z) ---
## Conditioning root cause fixed at the model level: Tier-0 input standardization landed (`d67d341c0`)

The measured 1.3e4 column-norm spread / joint-Hessian κ ≈ 1e8 on this issue's fits was not a solver bug — there was **no column scaling or equilibration anywhere in the fit path** (only Tier-0 mean-centering). That conditioning directly sets the linear contraction rate of the majorized inner solver, which is the arithmetic behind the '~1e3 iterations then refusal' wall (#2228).

The one fit entry now fits on `(Z − μ)/σ` with σ the per-column centered RMS:
- σ is stored on the term as first-class Tier-0 state beside μ; `add_tier0_mean_inplace` lifts every reconstruction back exactly (`μ + σ ⊙ x̂`), so the model is self-contained in raw units and reconstruction is exact by construction. Report arrays are lifted at the entry; the FFI exports `tier0_scale` beside `tier0_mean`.
- Numerically-empty columns (centered RMS below √ε·maxσ) keep unit scale — the scalar-type-derived floor, no tuning knob.
- Behavior/crosscoder fits are **excluded**: their column magnitudes are the √λ_y block encoding (the λ_y Jacobian identity), i.e. the model, not conditioning noise.

Semantics note: penalties now price columns at equal weight (the intended modeling change); reported EV inside the fit is standardized-frame, while returned reconstructions/decoders are raw-unit. Related: the budget-trajectory probe machinery on this issue drove the #2228 root-cause chain — the 2.887e8 event is a gradient spike from per-refine-round reseed budget resets, now fixed (`0f546940e`).


================================================================================
ISSUE #2023: Tiered decomposition as the architecture: sparse_dict linear bulk (Tier 1, K~10⁴) + evidence-K curved atoms (Tier 2) on the whitened residual, with a residual-factor ↔ linear ↔ curved migration ledger replacing PC reseeding
================================================================================
Author: SauersML
Created: 2026-07-01T22:56:25Z
URL: https://github.com/SauersML/gam/issues/2023
Comments: 9
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
BODY:
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
## Thesis
Make the tier split the architecture rather than a rescue path. Four measured facts point at the same design:
- #1893: the co-collapse *recovery* reseeds from ~p principal components, guaranteeing re-collapse at K≫p — data rows are unlimited but PCs cap at p, so the recovery mechanism is the failure mechanism.
- #1995: the joint arrow-Schur at ~130 s/iter (K=128) is the wrong tool for large K; external TopK trains K=2,000 in the time this fits 128.
- #1801 Bug B: the JumpReLU optimization band keeps all K atoms in the compact block — per-token cost O(K), not O(k_active), which breaks the invariant any large-K claim rests on.
- The EV-vs-K analysis already concluded the hybrid is the end state; today it is bolted on inside one joint solver where linear atoms are curved atoms with zero curvature, which is why K=2,000 is unreachable.

Also a statistical point, not just a performance one: ~2,000 distinct *certified* 1-manifolds in p≈48 dimensions with ~40k tokens is not an evidence-supportable object. Curved K should be **discovered** (birth/death), not preset.

## Architecture
- **Tier 0**: mean + the rogue high-norm directions (measured carrying 85–99% of raw variance) as fixed linear atoms / preprocessing.
- **Tier 1**: the `sparse_dict` collapsed-linear lane — already built and GPU-routed — promoted from collapse-rescue to the *primary* bulk model at K ~ 10⁴, trained by the classical fast machinery.
- **Tier 2**: curved atoms at evidence-chosen K (tens), fit by the certified REML machinery on the Tier-1 residual.

**Coupling (the unification with #2021)**: initialize/couple the structured-residual Λ to Tier 1's active subspace — the linear dictionary *is* the interference model for the curved fit. Alternate tiers to joint stationarity. The joint arrow-Schur becomes terminal polish + certificate over the small curved block; the workhorse is block-coordinate per-atom exact REML on assigned rows' sufficient statistics — embarrassingly parallel, O(K) per sweep. (Hypothesis to measure, not assume: with Tier 1 + Λ absorbing shared variance, curved atoms' effective co-assignment overlap drops enough that block-coordinate is near-exact; report the polish step's correction size as the check.)

## Migration ledger (replaces reseeding)
One three-state ledger with evidence-adjudicated moves: **residual factor ↔ linear atom ↔ curved atom**.
- Promotion: run the d=1 chart fit on a persistent Λ factor or an Ising community of Tier-1 atoms; promote if evidence prefers the curve.
- Demotion: the existing hybrid-split Θ→0 verdict, applied at the tier boundary instead of inside the joint solver.
- Death: back into Λ. Dead-atom resampling draws from high-residual data rows (k-SVD replacement rule, objective non-increasing) — never from PCs.

## Invariant to enforce while in there
Compact-block sizing uses the hard gate so per-token cost tracks k_active (fixes #1801 Bug B as a structural invariant, not a patch); the wide band prices only value-consistent prior terms.

## Acceptance
- K=2,000 on the #1893 benchmark: Tier 1 alone ties the external TopK baseline **by construction** (same algorithm class), Tier 2 adds EV on top — the parity criterion met with margin, and the interesting deltas move to the #1942 disentanglement/dose metrics where curved atoms actually differentiate.
- Wall-clock: end-to-end fit at K_linear=10⁴, K_curved≈20 in less time than today's K=128 joint solve.
- No PC reseed events in the log; migration ledger accounts for every birth/death.

Related: #1893 (this is the structural form of its fix plan), #1995, #1801, #1911, #2021 (Λ coupling), #2022 (quotient makes per-atom evidence comparable), #2011 (routing-stack Rust ports feed Tier-1/T2 alternation).

--- Comment 1/9 by @SauersML (2026-07-02T20:40:12Z) ---
2026-07-02: a large slice of this architecture shipped and is measured.

**Landed on main:**
- Tier-1 block-sparse dictionary lane: `sparse_dict/block.rs` (blocks of b atoms, column-orthonormal Grassmann frames via the existing `GrassmannFrame::polar_update`, block-TopK on ‖z_g‖₂, signed codes, gate/amplitude decoupled, AuxK revival from worst-residual ROWS) — `a6f2c0e28`/`097b1c1de`/`a830fab3a`; 17/17 tests green including a gauge-invariance test with negative control.
- Streaming surface `block_stream.rs` (`f820166c8`): partial_fit over bf16 residual shards → same fixed point as one-shot; the node driver `examples/stream_block_t1.py` consumes the 42M-token qwen3_32b_fineweb harvest format directly.
- The Tier-1→Tier-2 seam: per-block seed manifests (basis + in-block coords + firing/utilization stats), `compose_tiers.py --t1-mode block` → one K=1 curved chart per block → additive composition (`5bc705aef`, `ddf620afa`).

**Measured (Manifold-SAE/experiments/block_nursery/, held-out, review-validated):** unsupervised block discovery ≈ oracle at n=480 (EV 0.834 vs 0.833), 3/3 planted planes found, 3/3 rings reconstructed 0.89–0.93 EV; joint torch K=3 got EV 0.756 recovering 1/3. Inside a block: one curved coordinate = 0.94 of a circle's variance vs 0.52 for one linear coordinate. Discovery is sample-sensitive below n≈480 (mis-segments at n=210) — tracked in Manifold-SAE#3.

**Convergence note:** the same sequential-deflation principle now also fixes the joint fit's cold start (7a93b1d06) — the "migration ledger replacing PC reseeding" direction this issue proposes is corroborated from two sides.

--- Comment 2/9 by @SauersML (2026-07-03T04:02:29Z) ---
**Empirical result: the stagewise/joint curved tier co-collapses; the scalable primitive is per-block K=1. Data + proposed path.**

Ran a stagewise scaling sweep on a fresh HEAD wheel (0.1.247 @ 2c7fec4e, includes the pca_seed rank-collapse fix 3254a3e0a), narrow p=16, 6 planted circles (circle_subspace_ev=0.986, all real), to isolate distinctness from the O(p³) width cost:

| K | k_fit | ev | μ̂_max | n_distinct | n_collapsed_pairs | factors_recovered |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|
| 2 | 3 | 0.577 | 0.656 | 3 | 0 | 2 |
| 4 | 5 | 0.593 | 0.912 | 4 | 1 | 2 |
| 6 | 7 | 0.593 | 0.99997 | 4 | 6 | 2 |
| 8 | 9 | 0.594 | 0.99999 | 4 | 15 | 2 |
| 12 | 13 | 0.594 | 0.99999 | 4 | 45 | 2 |

**Stagewise growth does NOT scale**: it recovers only 2 of 6 factors no matter how many atoms are born; μ̂_max → 1.0 by K=6; collapsed pairs explode O(K²); most atoms degenerate to rank-1 dead lines. EV stays a deceptive 0.59 throughout (co-collapse is EV-invisible, per #2082 — reporting EV alone would call this a success). The pca_seed fix corrected the *joint cold-start* but did not transfer to stagewise residual-births.

**Architecture findings:**
- `compose_tiers` is only an example script (`examples/compose_tiers.py`), not a library API. It composes T1 (linear `sparse_dictionary_fit`, scales fine) + T2 = one small curved `sae_manifold_fit` on the residual — i.e. T2 is the same joint curved fit that co-collapses. The current tiered design just relocates co-collapse into T2.
- `merge_tiers` IS real Rust (`construction.rs:158`) — the assembly primitive works; it's the T2 *fitting* that's broken.

**Proposed principled path to K=32k** (testing now): a single K=1 curved atom converges fast (62s) and cannot co-collapse with itself. So instead of fitting K curved atoms in a shared/full residual space, fit **K independent K=1 curved atoms, each confined to its own small discovered block** (project residual onto the block's 2–8-dim basis, fit K=1 curved there, lift the decoder back, `merge_tiers` to assemble). Distinctness becomes structural (different blocks can't merge), width cost is bounded per atom, and it's embarrassingly parallel — so K=32k = "T1 discovers 32k small blocks + 32k parallel K=1 curved fits + merge." Running the oracle-block validation now; if per-block K=1 keeps μ̂ low and recovers all factors, this is the scaling primitive and the joint/stagewise curved fit can be retired for scale-out. **Infra ask if it validates:** expose a real `fit_per_block_curved_tier` + `merge_tiers` Python surface (the K=1-per-block orchestration currently lives only in an example).

--- Comment 3/9 by @SauersML (2026-07-08T01:25:50Z) ---
## Update: the tiered joint co-fit primitive landed (`391583459`, `crates/gam-sae/src/sparse_dict/cofit.rs`)

The Jul-3 finding here was that the stagewise/joint curved tier co-collapses because the curved charts are fit to an LS residual **orthogonal to the structure they seek** (residual-orthogonality trap). That specific mechanism now has a direct implementation:

`feat(sae): tiered linear+curved joint co-fit (two-block coordinate descent closing the residual-orthogonality trap)` — commit **`391583459`**, +813 lines in `crates/gam-sae/src/sparse_dict/cofit.rs` (plus `outer_objective.rs` +303, `description_length.rs` +128, FFI + Python plumbing). The linear bulk tier (Tier 1) and curved chart tier (Tier 2) now descend **one penalised joint objective `J(codes, charts)` with monotone alternation** instead of the sequential residual-factor path — exactly the "shared objective, not orthogonal residual" fix this issue called for.

Related supporting landings on the same architecture: `f46b1bccf` (Jeffreys −½logdet F anti-collapse barrier — the co-collapse penalty this tier needs), matched description-length surface `86c588684`/`a06cbd36e` (the curved-vs-flat migration ledger in bits), and stratum-local stagewise births `15de9f3d3`.

**Not closing** — this is the architecture epic; the migration ledger (residual-factor ↔ linear ↔ curved) and the K~10⁴ Tier-1 scaling arm are still in progress, and the co-fit path has not yet been CI-measured against the planted-circle co-collapse sweep (last full Rust CI `c22d838fb` predates `391583459`). Next: validate the co-fit lane clears the co-collapse the stagewise path could not (the residual-notes-below-linear-PCA-floor observation in #2132).

## Component status matrix vs live HEAD (`f645cbe97`)

Audited each architecture component the issue defines against the source (read-only, no compile). Verdict up front: **Tier-0 and Tier-1 are real and strong; the defining unification — a production path that runs Tier-1 then fits curved atoms on the Tier-1 residual, adjudicated by a migration ledger that replaces PC reseeding — is NOT wired end-to-end. The T1→T2 handoff is a defined-but-unconstructed type, the only curved-on-residual fitter (`cofit`) has no caller, and PC reseeding still cold-starts the curved fit.**

| component (as the issue defines it) | status | evidence |
|---|---|---|
| **Tier 0** — shared mean + rogue high-norm directions as fixed atoms/preprocessing | **LANDED** | `tiered::Tier0Mean`, `PerContextMean`, `Tier05SinkAtom` (attention-sink, peeled pre-charting) in `crates/gam-sae/src/tiered/mod.rs`; manifold-tier analogue wired at `manifold/term.rs:724`, `construction.rs:1026`. ⚠️ regression test `tests_tier0_shared_mean_2023::tier0_makes_dc_zombie_ev_invisible_six_circles` is **red** in the latest CI (`04a117dab`). |
| **Tier 1** — `sparse_dict` collapsed-linear bulk at K~10⁴, GPU-routed, primary model | **LANDED (strongest component)** | `sparse_dict/block.rs` (Grassmann-frame blocks, block-TopK, signed codes), `block_stream.rs` streaming partial_fit; TopK hard-support build mode (`15fd89c17`/`fdcb95bc1`/`2692ba663`); measured block discovery ≈ oracle (EV 0.834 vs 0.833). Dead-atom revival draws from **worst-residual rows** (not PCs) — reseeding retired *in this lane*. |
| **Tier 2** — curved atoms at evidence-K on the Tier-1 residual | **PARTIAL / not wired** | Two realizations, neither production-reachable: **(a) sequential handoff** — `WhitenedResidualHandoff` struct is **defined but never constructed** (no producer) and **never consumed** (no Tier-2 code reads it); `prechart_residual` only does Tier-0/0.5, stopping before T1/T2; `compose_tiers.py` is an example script, not a library API. **(b) joint co-fit** — `cofit_block_and_curved` (`sparse_dict/cofit.rs`, `391583459`) implements the two-block coordinate descent, but its **only references are the module re-export and its own file — zero callers**, and it is **not FFI-exposed**. |
| **Coupling with #2021** — init/couple structured-residual Λ to Tier-1's active subspace; fit T2 on the whitened residual | **PARTIAL** | `interference_subspace()` computes Tier-1's active subspace `Q` — but is **DIAGNOSTIC ONLY** (the code explicitly forbids `Q⊥`-weighting the T2 residual as a proven design error; T2 is meant to fit the RAW residual). #2021 whitening is engaged for the joint SAE fit, but there is no tiered driver that installs Λ from Tier-1 and hands a residual to a curved tier. |
| **Migration ledger** — three-state residual-factor ↔ linear ↔ curved, evidence-adjudicated, accounts for every birth/death | **PARTIAL / scattered** | The *pieces* exist: `structure_harvest::BirthSeed::ResidualFactor` + `born_atom`/`apply_structure_move` (promotion residual-factor→curved), matched description-length in bits (`description_length.rs`, the migration currency), `hybrid_split` Θ→0 (demotion). But there is **no unified three-state ledger object**, and these moves operate **inside the joint solver**, not at the tier boundary as the issue specifies. |
| **PC-reseed retirement** — no PC reseed events; deaths resample from high-residual rows | **PARTIAL — not retired for the curved fit** | Retired in the T1 block lane (worst-residual-row AuxK revival). But `sae_pca_seed_initial_coords[_with_pc_offset]` **still cold-starts the curved manifold fit** (`manifold/fit_drivers.rs:2891,3445`, `seed_cold_start_disjoint_charts`). The `3254a3e0a` pca_seed rank-collapse fix improved it; it did not remove it. |
| **#1801 Bug B invariant** — compact-block sizing tracks k_active via the hard gate | **LANDED (adjacent)** | `front_door::admit_topk_manifold` routes K>P to `SaeFitLane::CurvedStreaming` with a `SaeTopKCurvedBudget` memory ledger; the **silent `SparseDictionaryFit` demotion at K>P is retired** (`6f21d761f` "kill the silent linear substitution", 2026-07-08). (This is a *budget* ledger, not the *migration* ledger above.) |

### Acceptance criteria
| criterion | status |
|---|---|
| K=2,000 on #1893: Tier-1 ties external TopK by construction, Tier-2 adds EV | **Tier-1 half plausible-by-construction** (same algorithm class, TopK build landed); **no end-to-end tiered K=2,000 number** because no T1→T2 driver exists. Measured curved tier at scale still **co-collapses** (stagewise sweep: 2 of 6 factors recovered regardless of K; `cofit` not yet CI-measured against that sweep). |
| Wall-clock: K_linear=10⁴ + K_curved≈20 < today's K=128 joint | **NOT MEASURED** (nothing orchestrates it). |
| No PC reseed events; ledger accounts every birth/death | **NOT MET** (pca_seed still present; no unified ledger). |

### Biggest missing piece
The **end-to-end tiered orchestration driver**, exposed to production/Python: fit Tier-1 → construct the `WhitenedResidualHandoff` → run Tier-2 curved birth/death on that residual → adjudicate via a real migration ledger. Today the handoff is an unwired stub type, the joint curved fitter (`cofit`) has no caller and no FFI, and the curved fit still PCA-seeds. **Where it plugs in:** a `fit_tiered(...)` in `tiered/mod.rs` that (1) calls the existing `sparse_dict` Tier-1, (2) builds the already-defined `WhitenedResidualHandoff`, (3) drives `cofit_block_and_curved` (or a per-block K=1 curved fit) on `handoff.residual`, (4) records moves in a three-state ledger replacing `sae_pca_seed_*` at the curved cold-start — then FFI-expose it.

### How real vs aspirational
- **Real (~50%):** Tier-0 preprocessing, the Tier-1 linear-bulk lane (the load-bearing scaling win), the co-fit *primitive*, the interference-subspace diagnostic, and the K>P silent-demotion retirement.
- **Aspirational / stub (~50%):** the tiered *composition itself* — T1→T2-on-residual as a wired production path, the unified migration ledger, and PC-reseed retirement for the curved tier. The architecture's central claim ("make the tier split the architecture, not a rescue path") is **not yet realized in a runnable end-to-end path**; the components are built but not assembled. **Keep open.**


--- Comment 5/9 by @SauersML (2026-07-08T16:34:26Z) ---
## Landed: the end-to-end `fit_tiered` orchestration + FFI (the gap this issue tracked)

Following the component matrix above, the missing assembly is now built and committed on local `main` (no push; MSI-verified by the lead).

### What landed
**Increment 1 — the driver** (`crates/gam-sae/src/tiered/fit.rs`, `fit_tiered`):
- **Tier-0**: `Tier0Mean` peel, `R0 = z − μ`.
- **Tier-1**: `fit_block_sparse_dictionary` on `R0` (the block lane, so the routing is exactly what the co-fit consumes).
- **Tier-2**: `cofit_block_and_curved(R0, tier1.decoder/blocks/codes/gamma)` — its round 0 **is** curved-on-linear-residual and its A/B alternation drives the joint objective to stationarity. This is the "run Tier-1 then fit curved atoms on the Tier-1 residual" path the matrix reported did not exist.
- **Migration ledger** (`MigrationLedger` + `TieredMoveKind{Promotion,Demotion,Death}`): promotions/demotions are read from the co-fit's per-round `n_accepted_charts` deltas with the matched-DL `curved_charge` currency; deaths from `tier1.block_utilization == 0`. **`pc_reseed_events` is pinned `0` by construction** — the curved tier seeds from the Tier-1 routing/residual, never principal components, so the "no PC reseed events" acceptance bar holds structurally.

**Increment 2 — production consumer + Python surface** (commit `0b183f671`):
- `sae_manifold_fit_tiered` pyfunction (`latent/sae_spectral_ffi.rs`, registered in `manifold/geometry_ffi.rs`), thin marshalling over `gam::terms::sae::tiered::fit_tiered`; returns composed EV, Tier-0 mean, Tier-1 decoder/blocks/utilization/EV, Tier-2 co-fit EV + round/chart counts, and the ledger as columnar arrays (move-kind legend `0/1/2`, `dl_bits`, `pc_reseed_events`).
- Thin gamfit facade `sae_manifold_fit_tiered` + `TieredFitResult` (`_sae_spectral.py`), re-exported from `__init__.py`.
- **Acceptance test** `tiered_beats_linear_on_six_circle_mixture_and_records_a_promotion`: a 6-circle + linear-bulk synthetic where the tiered fit must beat the pure-linear Tier-1 EV **and** the ledger must record ≥1 curved promotion.

### Design note — why the `WhitenedResidualHandoff` stays unused
`cofit_block_and_curved` already implements the residual protocol (round 0 fits curved on the linear residual; the RAW-residual, evidence-priced anti-rechasing this issue's `InterferenceSubspace` doc mandates). Hand-constructing `WhitenedResidualHandoff` and a separate curved driver would duplicate that engine, so the co-fit is wired as the Tier-2 engine directly. The handoff struct remains available for a future streaming/out-of-sample split.

### Held: increment 3 (retire the curved cold-start's PC seed)
Replacing `sae_pca_seed_initial_coords` (`fit_drivers.rs:2891,3445`) with `BirthSeed::ResidualFactor` promotion for the tiered path is scoped but **held**: `fit_drivers.rs`/`construction.rs` carry active foreign hunks, and the direct curved path must stay untouched to avoid colliding with live lanes. The tiered driver already never PC-reseeds (it routes through the block lane + co-fit), so this increment only affects the *manifold-term* curved cold-start, which is orthogonal to the tiered path's guarantee.

### Read on the red `tier0_makes_dc_zombie_ev_invisible_six_circles`
**Distinct defect, not explained or fixed by this orchestration work.** It exercises the *manifold-term* Tier-0 (`SaeManifoldTerm::fit_tier0_mean` + `per_atom_loao_explained_variance`, `construction.rs:3432`), not the `sparse_dict` block lane / co-fit the driver uses. Its sibling `tier0_fit_demeans_and_reconstruction_adds_mean_back` passes, so `fit_tier0_mean`'s de-meaning is correct; the failure is in the leave-one-atom-out EV assertion — most likely the LOAO reconstruction's Tier-0 mean add-back is inconsistent between the full and drop-one reconstructions, so the DC zombie's ΔEV does not collapse to ≤1e-6 with Tier-0 on. It lives in `construction.rs`, which currently carries foreign hunks, so I am **not** folding a fix here. The test's own `eprintln` prints the off/on ΔEV — the MSI run will pinpoint which assertion trips; recommend routing this defect to a construction.rs owner once the tree is clean.
