--- Comment 7/9 by @SauersML (2026-07-11T04:10:25Z) ---
## K=2,000 acceptance measurement + tier0 gate status (MSI, pinned 8eb0b88c6)

### K=2,000 Tier-1 linear-bulk measurement — the acceptance number this issue asked for

Ran `examples/tiered_gpu_scale` (the composed `fit_tiered` spine that drives the block-sparse Tier-1 at high K) on MSI, 32-core CPU router, `--gpu off`. Device admission is `minibatch·K`-gated and below break-even here (`1,024,000 < 1,048,576`), so the CPU oracle is the honest portable baseline; the routing lane is byte-identical to the device path. Deterministic planted corpus: **N=32,768, P=64**, 8 shared linear directions + per-row wobble.

**K=2,000, block-size b=1 (== TopK by construction), block-TopK k=16:**

| epochs | wall (32 cores) | Tier-1 EV | frame-projector residual | fixed-point certified? |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| 3  | **16 s** | **0.8541** | 1.000 | no |
| 10 | 33 s | 0.8281 | 1.000 | no |
| 30 | 99 s | 0.7653 | 1.000 | no |

Comparison at the **same K=2,000, b=4** (500 blocks × 4), 30 epochs: EV 0.8272, frame residual 0.967, 77 s — also uncertified.

**Tie-by-construction: confirmed (algebraic).** At b=1 each block is a singleton, so the block gate `‖z_g‖₂` over a one-element slot is exactly `|z|` and block-TopK collapses to scalar TopK on the codes (`sparse_dict::block::stored_code_gate`). The K=2,000 b=1 run *is* a TopK SAE by construction, no approximation.

**Honest certificate caveat — a real, documentable finding.** The block lane's fixed-point certificate does **not** close at K=2,000 on this corpus, and EV *degrades* with epochs (0.854 → 0.765). Root: the corpus has intrinsic rank ≈ 8 but K=2,000 atoms, so ~1,984 atoms are spurious and perpetually under-utilised → dead-block AuxK revival reseeds a block's Grassmann frame onto worst-residual rows every epoch, flipping it orthogonally → the frame-projector fixed-point residual is pinned at ~1.0 (exactly 1.0 at b=1) and never reaches the 1e-6 tolerance, and the revival churn erodes EV. This is the **K ≫ intrinsic-rank / K ≫ active-budget** class (#2134-adjacent): the certificate is well-posed only when K is commensurate with recoverable structure. EV = 0.854 at 3 epochs is the best fixed point; further epochs churn rather than converge. The headline is **EV 0.854 at K=2,000, b=1, 16 s** with the certificate open for the stated structural reason.

**Tier-2 adds EV — not separately measurable on this corpus.** `fit_tiered` runs Tier-1 to a certified fixed point before handing its residual to the Tier-2 curved co-fit; since Tier-1 does not certify at K=2,000 here, Tier-2 never runs (the `--tier2` run reports the same Tier-1 error, 97 s). Independently, the example's planted data is purely **linear** (8 shared directions), so a curved Tier-2 has no curved structure to add on this corpus by design. A clean Tier-2-adds-EV measurement needs (a) a K commensurate with structure so Tier-1 certifies and (b) planted curved factors — flagging as the remaining measurement.

### Tier-0 gate (3 red tests) — roots found; all three are TEST-side, fixes landed

Exact status at 8eb0b88c6 (`--no-fail-fast`): `tier0_fit_demeans_and_reconstruction_adds_mean_back` **passes**; the other three fail. Both roots are test-side, not the deep convergence work.

**(1,2) `primary_entry_installs_tier0_mean_on_raw_target` + `primary_entry_tier0_is_a_noop_on_centered_target`.** These fit a K=1 Periodic atom to a clean 8-point circle, which reconstructs `[cosθ, sinθ]` to machine precision → pass-0 residual ≈ 0. The always-on **structured-residual outer pass** (`fit_entry.rs:555`, gated only on `structured_passes>0 && metric_provenance=="Euclidean"` — **not** on the tests' `run_outer_rho_search:false` / `run_structure_search:false`) then fits a residual-covariance model on ~0 residual: its idiosyncratic diagonal collapses to the denormal floor, whitening by ~1/D is near-singular, and the whitened REML over the 3 smoothing ρ has no interior stationary point → the outer optimizer **correctly refuses** to certify (`projected gradient 1.647e-1` vs `bound 5.018e-4`; confirmed by a direct gradient probe). Genuinely non-identifiable config, correct refusal — do not weaken the cert.

Fix (`dafd515d6`, test-config only): give the two fixtures real above-floor residual energy — a denser 64-point circle + small deterministic iid noise (σ = 0.05) — so the structured pass is well-posed. μ stays the exact column mean; the μ≈OFFSET / μ≈0 tolerances are widened to the noise's finite-sample band (std σ/√N ≈ 6e-3).

**(3) `tier0_makes_dc_zombie_ev_invisible_six_circles`.** The Tier-0 **headline property passes** (`DC-zombie ΔEV: off = 50.57 survivor, on = 0.0000 invisible`). The failure was a secondary check: each genuine circle's leave-one-atom-out ΔEV came out ≈ −0.14 (fixture expects ≈ +0.16). Root: the hand-built fixture loaded the periodic basis rows **swapped** — `PeriodicHarmonicEvaluator`'s column order is `[1, sin 2πt, cos 2πt]` (basis.rs:300), but the decoder put sin into the cos output dim and cos into the sin dim, so each circle reconstructed a swapped `(sinθ, cosθ)` circle uncorrelated with the target `(cosθ, sinθ)` → spuriously negative ΔEV. A test-fixture bug, **not** the `per_atom_loao_explained_variance` production defect previously suspected. Fix (`bc817f642`, test-fixture only): swap the two decoder rows.

MSI verification of all three at the combined HEAD is in flight; both fixes are landed on `main`.

### Production robustness bug surfaced (separate from #2023, worth a ticket)
The structured-residual pass runs on **every** SAE fit (magic-by-default) with **no absolute residual-energy floor** — so any real fit that explains its target near-exactly hits the same non-certification. Principled guard: `sae_structured_residual_model` returns `None` when total residual energy is below an absolute precision/noise floor (nothing to whiten → degrade to the pass-0 iid fit), or an absolute floor on the idiosyncratic diagonal in `residual_factor.rs`. Owner TBD (fit-driver surface).


--- Comment 8/9 by @SauersML (2026-07-11T16:02:15Z) ---
### Residual mechanical gap: sparse_dict has no CPU small-block baseline path

From the wide-p feasibility deep-dive (#2134 closed its p/N-scaling and top_k>1 walls; this one is the honest remainder):

`route_minibatch_required` (`crates/gam-sae/src/sparse_dict/scoring_gpu.rs:568,606`) **refuses any block with `m·k < DEVICE_SCORE_BLOCK_MIN_ELEMS = 1048576`** (`scoring_gpu.rs:435`). The guard lives in *routing*, so `score_mode="off"` does not lift it. Net effect: a small-K CPU baseline cannot run through the transform lane (the Python default `required` overrides the flipped FFI default), which blocks small-K CPU A/B comparisons against the frontier.

A `score_block_cpu` path already exists (`crates/gam-sae/src/sparse_dict/mod.rs:79`), so the fix is either:
- a documented minimum-K contract, or
- route small blocks (`< DEVICE_SCORE_BLOCK_MIN_ELEMS`) to `score_block_cpu` instead of fail-closed.

CPU-verifiable, low-risk — but it changes a **deliberate GPU fail-closed device contract**, so it wants an explicit decision rather than a silent flip.

For contrast, the wide-p **cubic-in-width cost is already retired**: Grassmann frames (`ensure_decoder_frames_active_for_current_decoder`, engaged on all three drivers) make the arrow-Schur border p-independent — p=4096 measured border 32768→64, cov 8.59 GB→32 KB (MSI job 12943297). The remaining wide-p cost is iteration *count*, not width (see #2080).


--- Comment 9/9 by @SauersML (2026-07-11T18:27:37Z) ---
Stage-5 pointer from the convergence-repair campaign: with the inner wall fixed at source (#2228 terminal Newton, Tier-0 standardization, EFS-everywhere routing), the remaining default-path cost/failure structure is the bundled pipeline — topology race × 2 whitening passes (each a new likelihood + full outer re-search) × structure search, multiplying both wall time and failure probability (#2267). The audit's conclusion matches this issue's tiered architecture exactly: make the tiered schedule the K>small entry (linear bulk + evidence-K curved atoms on per-block residuals, per-block confinement), and unbundle `sae_manifold_fit` to seed → single certified fit with race/whitening/births as explicit composable stages. Per-block confinement is also the structural fix for the K≥2 cold-joint co-collapse class and the #2260-style latent wander that EV cannot detect (cross-seed concordance is the reporting gap there). Recording here since this issue owns the architecture.

BODY:
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
The K≥2 inner-solve co-collapse is fixed (7a93b1d06, #2027 repro 3/3 green at p=16 and p=96), but the **outer** REML rho-search hang at wide p is a distinct, still-open surface.

**Data:**
- Real activations, p=16, n=95 (weekday+month, L8): `sae_manifold_fit` K=2 **converged in 61 s** (ev 0.47) — `Manifold-SAE/experiments/block_nursery/real_results.json`.
- Synthetic planted 3-circles, p=96, n=480: K=3 REML control **TIMEOUT_BLOCKED at 120 s**, no return — `Manifold-SAE/experiments/block_nursery/synthetic_results.json`.
- Prior fingerprints at width: non-PD cross-row IBP joint Hessian ("infeasible ρ probe"), BFGS Strong-Wolfe failures, #1026 incumbent-restore oscillation (W5/W6 node runs).

**Method question:** the hang lives in the outer `reml_criterion`/BFGS layer (non-PD retries at each ρ probe), NOT in `run_joint_fit_arrow_schur`. The inner fix means each criterion evaluation should now start from a separated cold seed — the outer loop may simply need (a) non-PD ρ-probe handling that fails fast instead of retrying, and/or (b) reusing the cold-start chart seeds across ρ probes instead of reseeding per probe.

**Acceptance:** a width-scaled test (plant 2 circles at p=96, full outer REML path) that completes within a bounded iteration count — no wall-clock budget per SPEC-18, but bounded probe count. Then the staged node rerun of the block_nursery REML control validates on real hardware.

--- Comment 7/27 by @SauersML (2026-07-03T03:19:49Z) ---
**Triangulation probe (MSI 12437107) — the "wide-p hang" is the K≥2 co-collapse surfacing at the OUTER solver. Full mechanism below.** All arms on the verified fresh 0.1.247 wheel, planted product-of-circles, n=480.

**p=16, K=1 → CONVERGES in 61.6s** (n_atoms=1). So the canned "hangs even at K=1" note was FALSE — single-atom is fine. But it converges *dirty*: Strong-Wolfe fails → backtracking fallback; a cost-stall "STUCK (not a flat valley)" escape; and a final **`CERTIFICATE warning: GRADIENT-OBJECTIVE DESYNC` (grad·v=−1.7e−2 vs fd·v=−1.17e−1, z=2.6e5)**. That desync is the fingerprint of the analytic logdet/adjoint derivative bugs being tracked in #2087 (red-tree localized 5 of them) — the fitter's own optimality self-audit is flagging the same wrong gradient.

**p=16, K=3 → FATAL in ~7 min** with `RemlConvergenceError` (not a plain hang). The mechanism, from the live log:
- The structural coherence detector fires on **every** atom pair — (0,1),(0,2),(1,2) all decode a **shared output subspace, μ̂=1.0000** (derived random-subspace null far below) — i.e. textbook co-collapse.
- Critically this happens at **healthy EV=0.9468** — the collapse is EV-invisible, exactly as #2082 established.
- The collapsed configuration is a degenerate outer geometry, so BFGS can't find a feasible step: `[OUTER] probe-refusal non-termination guard fired after 25 consecutive infeasible cost probes with no accepted gradient step (nan_seed=true)` → escalates to Fatal. Startup validation then reports all seeds `rejected_by_objective`.

**So #2080 ("wide-p REML hang") and the K≥2 co-collapse are the same problem seen at the outer-REML level.** The wide-p timeout is the co-collapsed, degenerate optimization thrashing infeasible probes until the wall cap; at p=16 it aborts fast, at p=96 it runs out the 40-min clock. The cold-start chart-deflation fix (`7a93b1d06`) is NOT preventing it in this joint `sae_manifold_fit(K=3, n_iter=40, random_state=0)` path — the seeds fail outer startup validation before/despite the deflation seeding, `nan_seed=true`. p96_K1 arm still running (isolates pure width from K).

Two concrete workstreams fall out: (1) the analytic derivative bugs (#2087) are not cosmetic — they desync the gradient the outer solver trusts, visible even in the converging K=1 case; (2) the cold-start disjoint-chart seeding needs to actually engage (or the outer startup-validation needs to accept it) in the joint multi-atom path, not just the tests_cocollapse_2027 entry path.

--- Comment 8/27 by @SauersML (2026-07-03T03:42:26Z) ---
**Triangulation complete — TWO independent failure modes, not one. Full table (fresh 0.1.247 wheel, planted circles, n=480):**

| | K=1 | K=3 |
|---|---|---|
| **p=16** | CONVERGES 61.6s | FATAL ~7min (co-collapse: all pairs μ̂=1.0, 25 infeasible outer probes) |
| **p=96** | TIMEOUT (600s cap) | TIMEOUT (900s cap) |

The load-bearing new datum is **p96_K1 timing out**. A single atom cannot co-collapse with itself, so this is NOT the co-collapse surface — it's a pure **width-scaling** cost in the outer REML / inner solve. 62s at p=16 → does not return in 600s at p=96 (6× width). The REML criterion's dense p×p logdet/Hessian work scales ~O(p³), so this is cubic-in-ambient-width. At real-data width (d=2048) a direct curved fit is intractable by orders of magnitude, independent of any co-collapse.

**So #2080 decomposes into two separable problems:**
1. **Co-collapse** (multi-atom) — degenerate shared-subspace geometry kills the outer solver even at narrow p. Owned by the disjoint-seeding-engagement work.
2. **Cubic width cost** (per-atom) — even K=1 is intractable at wide ambient p.

**Architectural consequence for scaling (K=32k):** curved atoms must NEVER be fit in the full ambient space. They must operate on **small per-block subspaces (d≈2–8)** — which is exactly the tiered design (block-sparse Tier-1 reduces dimensionality; curved Tier-2 refines within each small block). The tiered architecture isn't just elegant, it's *required* by the cubic width cost — a single curved atom in 2048-dim ambient is already too slow, let alone 32k of them. Both failure modes are dissolved by keeping curved fits low-ambient-dimensional and growing atoms stagewise rather than jointly.

Even the converging p16_K1 case emits `CERTIFICATE warning: GRADIENT-OBJECTIVE DESYNC` (the #2087 analytic-derivative fingerprint), which likely worsens the width-scaling thrash — wrong gradients make the outer solver take tiny/infeasible steps that compound as p grows.

--- Comment 9/27 by @SauersML (2026-07-03T04:07:59Z) ---
**Correction to the "cold-start disjoint seeding does NOT engage in the joint path" claim — it DOES engage; the real mechanism is entanglement-specific.**

I built a faithful K=3-circle repro through the REAL `OuterProblem` (`seed_budget=1, max_seeds=1`, exactly as `sae_manifold_fit_minimal` drives it — confirmed the FFI entry passes a COLD zero-init decoder + PCA seed coords, ffi line ~6782), instrumented the entry gate in `run_joint_fit_arrow_schur` (`max_decoder_norm==0 ⇒ cold-seed fires`), and measured structural distinctness (per-atom decoder norms + `structural_coherence_collapse_detected`), not EV. Findings at HEAD `2c7fec4ef`:

1. **The cold-start `seed_cold_start_disjoint_charts` DOES fire in the real outer path.** On the FIRST ρ probe `max_decoder_norm==0`, so entry seeding runs and places disjoint decoders (norms e.g. `[18, 25, 11]`). It is NOT rejected at startup validation before deflation. The earlier "seeds rejected before disjoint deflation / nan_seed before it engages" reading was wrong.

2. **It fires exactly ONCE per fit.** Every subsequent ρ probe sees the warm decoder (`fired=false`), so there is no re-seeding across the ρ-search — no recovery if an atom later drifts toward collapse.

3. **On DISJOINT-subspace planted circles (what `tests_cocollapse_disjoint_2027` uses), atoms separate and converge at every scale I could run** — direct `run_joint_fit_arrow_schur` gives `coherence=None` with all atoms carrying material norm up to `(n=480, p=16)` and `(n=240, p=96)`; the full outer path converges `Ok` at n=45 (EV=0.478, separated). The co-collapse is **not reproduced by disjoint circles at all**.

4. **The differentiator is DATA STRUCTURE, not the seeding wiring.** This issue's data is a *product-of-circles* — an ENTANGLED / overlapping-frame manifold. With overlapping frames, the seed's sequential PCA-**residual** deflation (atom 0 = dominant factor of the target, atom 1 = dominant of the residual, …) cannot cleanly peel one circle at a time, so later atoms get degenerate seeds. Measured: with entangled/overlapping-frame data the weakest-to-strongest decoder-norm ratio collapses from **~0.42 (disjoint)** to **~0.13 (entangled p=16)** / **~0.16 (entangled p=48)**, EV 0.49→0.35 — the onset of co-collapse (the 3rd atom is squeezed out).

**Root diagnosis.** The disjoint-chart seed's separation ASSUMES the planted factors are peelable in disjoint subspaces — true for the test fixture, FALSE for an entangled product manifold — AND it fires once at entry with no mid-ρ-search re-engagement (the `structural_coherence_collapse_detected` detector that would catch drift is telemetry-only per #2082 because it false-positives on healthy correlated atoms).

**Honest limitation.** I could NOT reproduce the full `μ̂=1.0` / EV=0.9468 collapse at `(n=480, p=96)` on the laptop — a ~30s wall-clock reaper SIGKILLs fits that large. The entangled-data trend points straight at it; full-scale confirmation (and a rigorous T³-product generator; mine is a coupled multi-phase curve on overlapping frames) needs MSI, which the red-tree lane is set up to run.

**Implication.** Joint K≥2 curved genuinely WORKS for disjoint/peelable factors and degrades on entangled structure. This favors the tiered + STAGEWISE route (peel one factor → deflate → repeat, and/or per-block K=1) over joint fitting for entangled manifolds. The open question the per-block experiment answers: does confining each atom to its own small block subspace RESCUE the entangled case, or does the entanglement contaminate the projected block too?

Self-contained Rust repro (disjoint + entangled generators, direct-vs-outer paths, entry-gate instrumentation) available for the MSI full-scale run.
---

**Correction (framing, thanks to the red-tree lane).** Scratch "favors the STAGEWISE route for entangled" above — that's wrong. Red-tree's data shows **stagewise peel-deflate births ALSO co-collapse on the entangled product-of-circles** (2/6 factors, μ̂→1.0). That's expected in hindsight: stagewise is the SAME peel-and-deflate mechanism as the joint-entry disjoint seeding, just sequenced across births — so it inherits the same failure, deflating one factor from an entangled manifold leaves a residual that still entangles the rest. So the accurate statement is: **peel-and-deflate (joint-entry seeding OR stagewise) works for DISJOINT factors and degrades on ENTANGLED**, independent of sequencing. The open rescue for entangled is therefore NOT stagewise — it's **structural per-block CONFINEMENT** (project onto a small block subspace, fit K=1 there) or a **non-disjoint (whitened joint-diagonalization / ICA-like) seed** that doesn't assume peelability. The per-block-K=1-on-entangled experiment (red-tree, MSI) decides which.


--- Comment 10/27 by @SauersML (2026-07-03T04:54:47Z) ---
**Cross-ref from #2089** — a concrete, actionable measurement of the intra-fit time sink, and where the fast-refuse belongs.

While closing the #2089 process-kill (memory-safety part fixed by `7a93b1d06`; a strictly-gated defense-in-depth bail landed in `0f1efbeff`), I profiled *where* a totally-co-collapsed K≥2 fit spends its wall time. It is **not** the outer ρ-search retrying many probes — for the tiny repro (n=120, p=32, K=6, `ibp_map`/circle) the death is **intra-probe**: each co-collapse reseed cycle inside a single `run_joint_fit_arrow_schur` call spends **~10–13 s** in the inner `(t, β)` solve thrashing on the near-degenerate / non-PD co-collapsed system — the "`[#1026] restoring inner-fit reconstruction incumbent after EV degraded …`" churn — so the 3-reseed multi-start budget isn't exhausted for ~35 s.

That contradicts the inner solve's own contract: the `probe_outer_criterion_value` / `is_recoverable_value_probe_refusal` comments state an infeasible/degenerate ρ should "return the typed refusal after a single diagnostic pass" (defect-2 in the #2080 notes). Empirically, on a *provably* degenerate co-collapsed inner system it does **not** single-pass-refuse — it grinds the damped LM / proximal-ridge Newton to the iteration cap while the reduced Schur stays indefinite (the `schur_pd_floor` engages but the loop still crawls).

Actionable, SPEC-18-clean fix for this lane (convergence-gated, not a timer): detect the *provably* non-PD / rank-deficient inner `(t, β)` system up front (the reduced-Schur indefiniteness is already computed) and return the typed infeasible-ρ refusal in **one** diagnostic pass, instead of letting the LM loop inflate ρ_β over thousands of tiny steps. The whitened-metric + anchor-birth prevention work (#2023) should also shrink how often this path is hit. Once the per-cycle cost drops from ~10 s to a single pass, the #2089 defense-in-depth bail reaches reseed-exhaustion quickly and raises its diagnostic, and this wide-p outer hang shortens correspondingly.

Not fixing it here (out of the #2089 bail-out scope) — flagging with the measurement so the co-collapse-solver lane can pick it up.

--- Comment 16/27 by @SauersML (2026-07-09T01:15:47Z) ---
## Wide-p per-eval cost: where it actually is, and a desync-safe sub-quadratic construction

Follow-up to the four-lever train (50aae88fb) — the hang is fixed, so what remains is the per-eval cost that makes #2230's phases run for hours (~5 min/criterion-eval at p=7168). This comment pins the cost to the right term and derives the construction that removes it without re-opening the objective↔gradient desync class.

### 1. The wall is the dense Schur *assembly*, not the Cholesky

At the accepted stationary iterate the evidence log-det path does (newton_step.rs:131-133):

- `build_dense_schur_direct`: `S = H_ββ − Σ_i H_βt^(i) (H_tt^(i))⁻¹ H_tβ^(i)`, cost **O(n·q·k²)** with `k = Σ_k M_k·p` (border dim), `q` = per-row coordinate dim;
- `factor_dense_reduced_schur`: **O(k³/3)**.

At #2230 phase-1 shapes (p=7168, K=1 circle ⇒ M=3, k≈21.5·10³, n=6·10⁴, q≈2-3):

- assembly ≈ n·q·k² ≈ **10¹³·⁵–10¹⁴ flops**,
- Cholesky ≈ k³/3 ≈ **3·10¹² flops**.

So the assembly term is ~20-30× the factorization. Any fix that still *forms* S dense (better factorization, low-rank *corrections* to a formed S, GPU Cholesky) leaves the dominant term standing. The escape must be **matrix-free in S**.

A matrix-free matvec is cheap by comparison:

`S·v = H_ββ·v − Σ_i H_βt^(i) (H_tt^(i))⁻¹ (H_tβ^(i) v)` costs O(Σ_i q_i·k) ≈ n·q·k ≈ **3·10⁹ flops** — four orders of magnitude below one assembly. The per-row `H_tt` factors are already computed for the gradient path, so the matvec has no new factorization cost.

(For the record, the exact determinant-lemma route — write the row corrections as a rank-`Σq_i` update and use `log|S| = log|H_ββ| + log|I − U^T H_ββ^{-1} U|` — is only sub-dense when `n·q ≪ k`. That holds for the tiny-N probe lanes (N≈180 repros) and could be wired there, but at n=6·10⁴, `n·q ≈ 1.2-1.8·10⁵ > k`, so it cannot serve real fits. Not the road.)

### 2. Why plain SLQ was rightly kept off the CPU criterion path

`slq_logdet.rs` exists (32 Rademacher probes, device-gated ≥4096). The reason it must not be dropped naively into `reml_criterion`: the outer solve consumes **both** the value ½log|S| and its analytic ρ-gradient. If the value is a stochastic estimate and the gradient is the exact trace channel (which is exact today — the #2087 audit confirmed the trace channel), the line search descends on a function whose gradient belongs to a *different* function. That is precisely the obj↔grad desync genus this repo has been burned by repeatedly. Fresh probes per eval are even worse: the criterion becomes noise on the scale of the stall tolerances.

### 3. The desync-safe construction: a *fixed* rational surrogate, differentiated exactly

Fix, per outer solve (not per eval):

- probe block `V = [v_1 … v_m]`, Rademacher, **common random numbers across every ρ evaluation**;
- a rational approximation of log on a spectral bracket `[a, b] ⊇ spec(S(ρ))`:
  `log x ≈ r(x) = c₀ + Σ_{ℓ=1}^{L} w_ℓ · x/(x + t_ℓ)` (any of the standard forms works; the Hale–Higham–Trefethen conformal-map quadrature gives geometric convergence, L = O(log κ · log 1/ε), so L ≈ 25-40 covers κ up to 10¹² at ε = 10⁻⁶).

Define the **surrogate criterion term**

&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;`L̃(ρ) = (k/m)·Σ_j v̂_jᵀ r(S(ρ)) v̂_j`,&nbsp;&nbsp; v̂ normalized probes,

computed with shifted-CG: one Krylov space per probe serves **all L shifts** `(S + t_ℓ I)⁻¹ v_j` simultaneously.

The point of the construction: `L̃` is a *deterministic, smooth* function of ρ (probes and quadrature fixed), and its **exact** ρ-gradient is

&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;`∂L̃/∂ρ = (k/m)·Σ_j Σ_ℓ w_ℓ t_ℓ · y_{jℓ}ᵀ (∂S/∂ρ) y_{jℓ}`,&nbsp;&nbsp;`y_{jℓ} = (S + t_ℓ I)⁻¹ v̂_j`

— computable from the **same** shifted solves as the value, plus matrix-free `(∂S/∂ρ)·y` matvecs (differentiate the per-row contributions; same row loop as the existing trace channel). Value and gradient are now the same function by construction: **the desync class is closed off structurally, not by tolerance tuning.** The outer BFGS optimizes L̃ exactly; Wolfe conditions are meaningful; the stall certificates apply verbatim.

Bias control is a *terminal* concern, not a per-eval one: E_V[L̃] = tr r(S) and the probe fluctuation is a fixed smooth O(m^{-1/2}·‖·‖) perturbation of the criterion surface, so ρ̂ is perturbed O(m^{-1/2}) — then certify once at ρ̂ with either (a) an independent probe block (bracket test), or (b) a single dense assembly+factorization at the terminal point only (one 5-minute eval per *fit* is fine; per *eval* is what kills).

### 4. Two refinements that come for free

- **Hutch++/deflation**: run a few subspace iterations (matvecs only) to peel the top-r eigenspace of S, take its log-det exactly, SLQ the deflated remainder. This (i) collapses the variance (the heavy tail of the spectrum is what Hutchinson variance lives on), (ii) shrinks κ and hence L, and (iii) *independently* neutralizes the 10⁵⁷-spread pathology that motivated e1aefbd3d — the same subspace that breaks reconstruct-then-refactor is the one you want deflated anyway.
- **Unit-deflation consistency**: the evidence convention (spectral_unit_deflated_schur) sends null/non-positive directions to `log 1 = 0`. In the matrix-free lane the identical convention is: bottom-subspace vectors discovered by the same subspace iteration are projected out of the probes and contribute 0 — same quotient pseudo-determinant, no ρ-dependent bias.

### 5. Cost model at #2230 phase-1 shapes

| term | dense path (today) | fixed-rational surrogate |
|---|---|---|
| per criterion eval | n·q·k² ≈ 10¹⁴ + k³/3 ≈ 3·10¹² | m probes × ~CG iters × (n·q·k) ≈ 32 × 60 × 3·10⁹ ≈ **6·10¹²** |
| per ρ-gradient | trace channel (existing) | reuses the same y_{jℓ}: + m·L (∂S/∂ρ)-matvecs |
| terminal certificate | — | one dense eval at ρ̂ |

≈ 15-20× per-eval reduction at these shapes before deflation/warm-starts (CRN probes make y_{jℓ}(ρ) smooth in ρ ⇒ warm-started CG converges in a fraction of the cold iters after the first eval — in practice the multiplier is much larger). It also removes the k×k dense allocation, which is what stops β_dim ≈ 10⁵ (the #1017 77 GB wall) from ever being reachable on the dense path.

### 6. Wiring sketch

1. `slq_logdet.rs`: add the fixed-probe/fixed-quadrature surrogate variant (probe block + bracket + quadrature stored per outer solve, e.g. on the ρ-search state next to ProbeConvergedHandoff).
2. Shifted-CG on the matrix-free `S`-matvec (per-row loop; H_tt factors reused from the gradient path). Multi-shift CG shares the Krylov basis across all t_ℓ.
3. `reml_criterion`: route k ≥ threshold (existing 4096 constant) through the surrogate on CPU as well as device; keep dense below.
4. Gradient: extend the existing per-row trace-channel loop to accept the y_{jℓ} bundle (it already knows ∂S/∂ρ row-locally).
5. Terminal: one dense assembly+factor at accepted ρ̂ as the certificate + the returned cache (so downstream consumers of the factor cache are untouched).

Cross-refs: #2230 (the hours-long phases are this per-eval cost), #1017 Phase-3 (the matrix-free matvec here is the same primitive the device-resident lane needs — build it once, host first, device second), #2087 (trace channel already exact; this construction keeps it consumed against a value of the same functional).

--- Comment 17/27 by @SauersML (2026-07-09T15:03:02Z) ---
## Wide-κ log-det surrogate has a real ~5% deterministic bias (not Hutchinson variance)

Settled the variance-vs-bias question for the deflated rational log-det surrogate in the wide-κ regime with a **96-seed frozen-Q discriminator** (`deflation_wide_kappa_variance_vs_bias_multiseed`, gam-solve `arrow_schur/rational_logdet.rs`). Each of 96 plans uses a different probe seed but the **same** frozen deflation basis Q (rank 16) and **exact** solves, so only Hutchinson probe noise varies across seeds; a bias that survives the seed-average is structural.

```
wide-κ (96 seeds, fixed Q, EXACT solves):
  exact    = 57.388446
  mean     = 60.258544
  bias     = +2.870098   (5.001e-2 rel, 5.57σ of the mean)
  seed sd  = 5.0478   se_mean = 0.5152   ⟨internal std_err⟩ = 8.5816
VERDICT: genuine DETERMINISTIC bias survives probe-averaging.
```

**Why an earlier single-draw check read this as "variance-dominated":** the per-draw internal std_err is **8.58** (~15% of |logdet|), so on one 32-probe draw the +2.87 offset is only ~0.3σ — invisible under the noise. Averaging 96 seeds shrinks the noise floor to se_mean=0.515, and the offset emerges at **5.57σ**. So the RED gate `deflation_cuts_..._wide_kappa` was correct all along; this is not a mis-calibrated bar.

**Consequence for the surrogate:** the fix is genuine derivation work on the log-det **value** surrogate — either the exp-sinh DE quadrature (node count / sinh-tail truncation at wide κ) or the term1/term2 split normalizer `c` in `tr(Qᵀ log(S/c) Q)` — **not** variance reduction (more probes / higher deflation rank won't remove a deterministic offset). The θ-adjoint gradient folds are orthogonal and unaffected (exact at full-basis, unbiased for any probe count). Fix in progress.

--- Comment 18/27 by @SauersML (2026-07-09T15:54:55Z) ---
## Retraction: the "+2.87 deterministic bias / 5.57σ" above was a probe-RNG aliasing artifact — it IS Hutchinson variance

The "Wide-κ log-det surrogate has a real ~5% deterministic bias" comment above (the 96-seed frozen-Q `deflation_wide_kappa_variance_vs_bias_multiseed` result) is **wrong, and I'm retracting it.** The offset was not a quadrature or split defect — it was an artifact of the probe RNG, and the original variance hypothesis is restored.

**Proof chain** (Python-replicated against the exact Rust spectrum + DE nodes, then confirmed in-tree):

1. **Pure DE quadrature is exact at κ=2.6e7**: Σ[Q(λ) − log(λ/c)] = −3e-10 over the full spectrum. No node-count / sinh-tail-truncation error.
2. **The term1/term2 split is exact**: for orthonormal Q, tr(QQᵀMP)=0; a full-rank deflation (rank = dim, projector P=0, i.e. *zero* Hutchinson) reproduces the exact log-det to 5e-12. So neither the split normalizer `c` nor the quadrature carries bias.
3. **The offset was RNG aliasing.** The old per-probe init set state = (seed+p)·γ, which makes the splitmix streams seeded at x₀ and x₀+γ the *same* stream shifted by one. Across 96 unit-spaced seeds the 3072 probe slots drew only **127 distinct probes** — each seed's estimate was a ~32-wide sliding-window mean of a shared pool, so the seeds were ~4-effective-independent, not 96. The sample-sd/√96 therefore **underestimated the true mean-standard-error by ~4.9×**, and 5.57σ ÷ 4.9 ≈ **1.1σ** — squarely within noise. There is no surviving deterministic offset.

**Verdict:** wide-κ error here is genuine **Hutchinson variance** (~16% of |logdet| on a single 32-probe draw), *not* a value-surrogate derivation bug. So the production lever is **variance reduction, not re-derivation**:

- Probe RNG fixed to a sequential `splitmix64_hash(seed)` master stream for both probes and the deflation start — restores cross-seed independence (>0.95·3072 distinct) while keeping per-seed CRN determinism.
- **Two-sided deflation** (`with_two_sided_deflation`): offdiag(log(S/c)) sits symmetrically on both spectral tails, so one-sided top deflation stalls at ~½lnκ. Peeling the bottom via inverse subspace iteration (matrix-free CG) as well drops calibrated std_err **7.23% → 1.49%** at |logdet|=57.4 (2.75× under equal-rank one-sided). Approx bottom-Q never biases (exact split for any orthonormal Q).

New discriminator gate `full_rank_deflation_is_exact_at_wide_kappa_deterministic_bias_localizer` (rank=dim, zero-noise, exact-Cholesky arm, asserts <1e-6) is the clean test the multiseed couldn't be. The θ-adjoint gradient folds are orthogonal and unaffected (exact at full-basis, unbiased for any probe count). Apologies for the earlier mis-call — the frozen-Q multiseed looked airtight but its own probe pool was aliased.

--- Comment 19/27 by @SauersML (2026-07-09T21:42:40Z) ---
## Defect-4 root-fix derivation (from the SPEC-conformance audit)

The `value_consistent_outer_gradient` FD safeguard (outer_objective.rs) is the one remaining production finite-difference (SPEC rule 2). Audit + code reading sharpened the root fix:

**Key structural fact**: `solve_exact_stationarity` runs left-`B`-preconditioned GMRES on `A = B + ΔC`, and `B ⪰ A` by construction (Gershgorin entropy majorizer, `max(V'',0)` ARD majorizers, GN data curvature). Therefore the preconditioned operator `B⁻¹A` has spectrum in `(0, 1]`, and the desync direction (saturated IBP gate logit, data curvature `∝ σ'(ℓ)² ≈ 0`) is precisely the `μ → 0` tail of that spectrum. `θ̂_ρ` picks up a `(vᵀg_ρ)/μ` amplification there, corrupting the `−½Γᵀθ̂_ρ` envelope term into a sign flip.

**Scale-free fix**: deflate the small-`μ` subspace of the *preconditioned* spectrum (a cutoff on `μ = curvature retained as a fraction of its own majorizer` is dimensionless and interpretable, unlike any absolute ridge). Matrix-free: harvest approximate small-`μ` Ritz vectors from the GMRES Krylov space itself (they emerge for free as the stagnating directions), project them out of the solve, and zero their envelope contribution. Justification: along `μ ≈ 0` directions the inner optimizer's iterate position is majorizer-dynamics-dominated, so the true criterion's realized `dθ̂/dρ` there is NOT `1/λ_A`-scaled — the FD gradient the safeguard currently trusts confirms this empirically (moderate slope).

Once the deflated solve makes the analytic gradient value-consistent by construction, the 2-probe + 2·d_ρ FD machinery demotes to a debug-only diagnostic (or deletes), closing the SPEC-2 violation.

Validation fixture already named in the code: planted-circle IBP K=1 (railed at the ρ=1 GeneralizedLinear anchor, EV ≈ 0.87 vs > 0.95).

--- Comment 20/27 by @SauersML (2026-07-09T22:14:32Z) ---
Status update on the wide-kappa 'quadrature/split bias' lane: RESOLVED as a non-bug; no derivation work is owed.

The rational-logdet split identity was hand-verified exact for any orthonormal Q (P/Q trace decomposition, per-probe ||u||^2 dimension counting, k*ln c bookkeeping), and the DE quadrature step/truncation bounds are correctly derived. The earlier '5.57 sigma deterministic bias' verdict was an artifact of splitmix probe-stream aliasing across unit-spaced seeds — the 96-seed battery drew ~128 distinct probe vectors instead of 3072, so a shared Hutchinson fluctuation was reported as deterministic bias. All fixed on HEAD: one sequential master probe stream, a probe-fingerprint independence guard that fails loudly on re-aliasing, and two-sided (top+bottom tail) deflation for the variance. The multiseed discriminator test (`deflation_wide_kappa_variance_vs_bias_multiseed`) now asserts probe-averaged unbiasedness on CI. Remaining wide-p work on this issue is the perf lane (cubic width cost / #2087 amplification), not the surrogate math.

--- Comment 21/27 by @SauersML (2026-07-09T23:35:57Z) ---
## Status: the wide-κ "5.57σ bias" is closed as PROBE-RNG ALIASING; two-sided deflation is now the production variance lever

Consolidating today's findings on the deflation lane:

**1. The "deterministic bias" was never a bias.** The multiseed discriminator's 96 unit-spaced seeds drew only ~128 distinct probe vectors instead of 3072 — the per-probe RNG init `(seed+p)·γ` made probe `p` of seed `s` bit-identical to probe `p+1` of seed `s−1` (a splitmix stream from `x₀+γ` is the same stream shifted). Averaging correlated draws collapses `se_mean`, so a shared Hutchinson fluctuation reported as "5.57σ deterministic bias". Fixed by sequential consumption from one hashed master stream (`338251381`); the multiseed test now fingerprints every probe's sign pattern and hard-fails if unit-spaced seeds ever re-alias, so this failure mode cannot silently return.

**2. The split algebra is sound.** With exact dense-Cholesky solves and frozen Q, the probe-averaged estimate is unbiased at κ=1e8 (`deflation_wide_kappa_variance_vs_bias_multiseed`); the exact-arm discriminator exonerates CG convergence as well. What remains at wide κ is VARIANCE: the Hutchinson bar is `√(2‖offdiag(P·log(S/c)·P)‖_F²)`, whose mass sits symmetrically on BOTH spectral tails, so top-only deflation removes at most half of it and stalls near ½·lnκ-scale bars.

**3. Production now peels both tails.** `rational_reduced_schur_plan_derived` had the two-sided design in its doc but still called one-sided `with_deflation`; the cutover (`892aaea3d`) splits the peel rank across the tails at equal total rank and gives the inverse-iteration (bottom-tail) basis build its own loose CG budget — documented as bias-free since the split `tr log(S/c) = term1(Q) + term2(P)` is exact for ANY orthonormal Q, so basis-solve error can only relax variance reduction. Evaluation-grade CG on the unshifted full-κ operator would burn √κ-scale iterations per column for nothing.

The `two_sided_deflation_drops_wide_kappa_std_err_below_two_percent` deliverable pins the bar below 2% of |logdet| at equal total rank; the full wide-κ set runs in the MSI verify battery. Remaining on this epic after the battery goes green: nothing on the math side — the surrogate's value, all four gradient channels, the θ-adjoint, and now the variance lever are landed.


--- Comment 22/27 by @SauersML (2026-07-10T02:22:35Z) ---
## Defect 4: deflation fix LANDED (f777df0f2) — CI is the validation gate

Implemented the root fix from the derivation above, in `solve_exact_stationarity` (construction_exact_hessian.rs):

- **Detector**: the solution's own generalized Rayleigh quotient `μ(x) = xᵀAx/xᵀBx`. Since `B ⪰ A` (majorizer construction) the pencil spectrum is `(0,1]`, and any near-null component in the rhs enters the solve with weight `1/μ`, so `μ(x)` collapses to `≈ μ_min` exactly when amplification occurred. Healthy solves pay one extra `A`/`B` apply and exit.
- **Direction recovery**: inverse-power iteration `v ← A⁻¹(Bv)` (the existing B-preconditioned GMRES is the `A⁻¹` apply), seeded by the corrupted solution itself — which is already dominated by the offending direction.
- **Deflation**: exact in the `(A,B)` eigenbasis with **no re-solve** — the amplified term of `x` along a B-normalized eigendirection is `v(vᵀBx)`, so subtracting the B-projection removes precisely the unidentifiable `1/μ` component and touches nothing resolved. Up to 8 directions per solve (`SAE_IFT_MIN_CURVATURE_FRACTION = 1e-8`, dimensionless fraction-of-own-majorizer).

**Validation**: adversarial test `ift_solve_deflates_saturated_gate_near_null_direction_2080` (construction_tests.rs) — saturates atom-1 gate logits at −40 on the tiny IBP fixture, asserts **non-vacuity first** (the RAW GMRES solve must collapse below the 1e-8 floor, i.e. the fixture genuinely reproduces the defect) and then that the production solve restores `μ ≥ floor` via a B-norm-non-increasing projection. Local runs were SIGKILLed twice by the box watchdog (concurrent build storm), so **CI is the gate**: a red on the non-vacuity assert means the fixture needs strengthening; a red on the deflation asserts means the fix needs iteration; green means the desync class is closed at the source.

**Follow-up once CI is green**: demote/remove the `value_consistent_outer_gradient` FD safeguard in outer_objective.rs (the last production finite-difference, SPEC rule 2) — with the envelope solve value-consistent by construction, the safeguard's stage-1/stage-2 probes should never trip; re-measure the planted-circle IBP K=1 EV (expect > 0.95 vs the railed 0.87).

--- Comment 23/27 by @SauersML (2026-07-10T15:01:03Z) ---
SPEC-conformance audit finding at `37eb3116c52f03ce336e08a635cf9c69523fdaa5`: the newly landed analytic IFT deflation still has a correctness hole before it can replace the production FD safeguard safely.

In `solve_exact_stationarity`, inverse-power refinement currently does:

- seed `v = x`;
- if `A⁻¹(Bv)` GMRES fails, silently `break` and keep that unrefined seed;
- B-normalize it and apply `x ← x − v(vᵀBx)`.

If refinement fails on its first solve, `v` is exactly the normalized `x`, so the projection deletes the **entire IFT response** (up to roundoff) and returns it as an analytic derivative. Invalid B-norms and zero/non-finite projections also silently break and return a still-sub-floor response. Negative `xᵀAx/xᵀBx` (an indefinite exact Hessian / non-minimum) is currently sent through the same “near-null” projection instead of being rejected.

Those are fallback semantics, not an analytic root fix: they can manufacture a finite gradient without a converged refinement and violate SPEC's no-fallback/converged-only contracts. I am replacing them with explicit convergence/invariant failures and a postcondition that no returned IFT response remains below the identifiable-curvature floor. The focused battery is submitted on MSI as job `12937006` (pinned to the SHA above): saturated-gate IFT, the full rational-logdet suite, and the #2080 outer-gradient gate.


--- Comment 24/27 by @SauersML (2026-07-10T15:13:53Z) ---
Acceptance audit found that the existing green #2080 fixtures were not enforcing SPEC's converged-fit contract. Both `wide_p_outer_reml_terminates_within_probe_budget_2080` and `entangled_two_circle_outer_reml_separates_2080` discarded `OuterResult.converged` and then extracted `objective.into_fitted()`; with `max_iter=4`, a finite positive-EV last incumbent could therefore pass even when outer REML had stopped nonconverged.

Landed and pushed `f98ef0cad` (`test(sae #2080): require converged outer fits`): the wide-p K=2/K=3 helper, the entangled K=2 fixture, and the adjacent K=1 livelock fixture now require `result.converged == true` before any fitted state or EV is accepted. Failures report iterations, final criterion, and final gradient norm. Bounded probe counts remain the performance gate; elapsed time is not asserted.

This may turn previously “green” acceptance red, but that red is load-bearing: #2080 is resolved only if the bounded wide-p/entangled paths return a certified converged optimum, not merely a usable-looking incumbent.


--- Comment 25/27 by @SauersML (2026-07-11T04:04:46Z) ---
## Wide-p perf scoping (deep trace, HEAD)

**The cubic-in-width border cost is resolved and engaged magic-by-default on the plain-SAE path — not just crosscoder.** All three drivers call `ensure_decoder_frames_active_for_current_decoder` (dense `fit_drivers.rs:4899`, streaming `fit_drivers.rs:6400`, crosscoder `crosscoder_fit.rs:848`). Per-atom Grassmann frames `B_k=C_k Uᵀ` activate at `p≥12` & `r≤0.75p`, so the arrow-Schur border carries `Σ_k M_k·r` (r≈8–32) instead of `Σ_k M_k·p`. Reduced Schur factorization and covariance become **p-independent**.

Measured (MSI job 12943297, commit 6d4cff82e, N=1500 p=4096): border `32768→64` (512×), covariance `8.59 GB→32 KB`, wall 4.35 s, MaxRSS 432 MB. The "O(p³) border Cholesky dies / 8.6 GB per atom" regime is gone.

**The remaining wide-p cost is iteration COUNT, not width.** On co-collapsed / near-singular geometry the inner Newton crawls a flat inter-atom gauge direction — each Armijo step lowers the objective sub-√εmach while ‖g‖ stays above tol — grinding the full ≥1024 inner `max_iter` at ~1 s/iterate, multiplied through the 6+ outer ρ probes. That is the K≥2 "hours-long hang," and it is a convergence-RATE problem, not a per-iterate p cost.

**Ranked perf levers (scoped):**
1. **Warm-start the inner joint fit across ρ probes** — today each criterion/fd probe cold-re-runs `run_joint_fit_arrow_schur` up to ≥1024 iterates; reuse the separated incumbent from ρ₀ as the seed for adjacent probes. `O(probes×1024×s)` → `O(probes×few×s)`.
2. **Fail-fast non-PD ρ probes** — a non-PD cross-row IBP Hessian at a probe should score infeasible-with-gradient and move the bracket, not retry into the inner budget (CPU-verifiable on the p=96 planted-circles fixture).
3. **Quotient the inter-atom shared-subspace gauge** at the inner level (analogous to the single-atom chart-gauge deflation at `fit_drivers.rs:1474`) so the grad/step gates clear at the true optimum instead of grinding — the deep root fix (research-grade).

Already landed and holding: K≥2 co-collapse fix (7a93b1d06), value-probe purity (cca741e3f), bounded probe budget (`wide_p_outer_reml_terminates_within_probe_budget_2080`: EV 0.9085, 6 criterion calls, 0 mutating probes), converged-gated acceptance (f98ef0cad).

================================================================================
ISSUE #2132: sae_manifold_fit dictionary co-collapses on planted circle mixtures (held-out EV low, decreasing in K, below linear PCA)
================================================================================
Author: SauersML
Created: 2026-07-04T22:01:58Z
URL: https://github.com/SauersML/gam/issues/2132
Comments: 10
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
BODY:
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
## Summary

On planted mixtures of clean circles, `sae_manifold_fit` (multi-atom dictionary) reaches
low held-out reconstruction EV that **decreases with K** (dictionary co-collapse), and
underperforms both a trivial linear-PCA baseline and its own linear-atom variant on the
exact curved structure it is designed to capture.

## Reproduction (gamfit 0.1.248)

Data: `N=1500` tokens, each lying on **exactly one** of `C` planted unit circles in a
random 2-plane of R^p (single-active, so top-1 routing is exact), 5% noise, 20% held out.
Fit `sae_manifold_fit(train, K, d_atom=1, atom_topology="circle"/"linear", top_k=1,
n_iter=12, _run_structure_search=False)`; score held-out EV via `reconstruct(test)`.

Measured (held-out EV; train `reconstruction_r2` in parens):

| regime | linear PCA @matched rank | curved (circle) | same-lane linear (`atom_topology="linear"`) |
|---|---|---|---|
| C=3, p=12, K=6 | ~0.73 (rank 3) | **0.23** (train 0.54) | — |
| C=6, p=24, K=6 | ~0.55 (rank 6) | **0.26** (train 0.37) | 0.25 (train 0.57) |
| C=6, p=24, K=8 | ~0.56 | **0.11** (train 0.46) | 0.25 (train 0.57) |
| C=8, p=48, K=6 | — | **0.23** (train 0.41) | — |

Two problems visible:
1. **Co-collapse**: curved held-out EV *drops* from 0.26 (K=6) to 0.11 (K=8) — more atoms
   make it worse. Inner-fit logs emit `[#1026] restoring incumbent` / `dictionary
   co-collapse ... reseeding all atoms`.
2. **Large train→held-out gap** (both lanes: train ~0.55 → held-out ~0.25), i.e. the
   out-of-sample encode/reconstruct path generalizes poorly, and curved atoms
   underperform even the linear-atom variant on curved data.

A linear PCA reconstruction at the matched rank reaches 0.55–0.73 on the identical data,
so the structure is trivially recoverable — this is a solver-quality gap, not a data
problem.

## Also (0.1.247 only)

`reconstruct(test)` on a circle fit raises
`sae_manifold_predict_oos: decoder_blocks[0] has M=2 but rebuilt basis has M=3` — the
trained decoder width and the OOS basis rebuild disagree (M=2 vs M=3). 0.1.248 is
consistent (M=3) and does not raise, but the held-out EV gap above suggests the OOS
encode path is still the weak point.

## Why it matters

This blocks a compute-matched curved-vs-linear dictionary frontier (curved cannot reach
the linear reconstruction ceiling here, let alone beat it at fewer atoms). The single-
chart `K=1` fits used in the dose-calibration work are unaffected; the failure is specific
to the multi-atom dictionary sweep. Harness + raw JSONs:
`SauersML/Manifold-SAE:experiments/frontier_bench.py`,
`results/suite_2026-07-03/frontiers/exact_p24_curved.json`.

--- Comment 1/10 by @SauersML (2026-07-04T22:05:56Z) ---
Clarification on the metric convention (accuracy): the load-bearing evidence is **held-out EV computed the same raw way** — `ev(test, reconstruct(test))` with SS around the test mean — for the curved chart, the same-lane linear atoms, AND the linear-PCA baseline, on the identical held-out split. On that consistent metric the curved dictionary sits at 0.23–0.26 (decreasing in K) vs linear-PCA 0.55–0.73.

The `train` numbers I quoted are gamfit's own `reconstruction_r2`, which is a **different (whitened/penalized in-model) convention** — not comparable to the raw held-out `ev()`. Concretely, one ambient-p=1024/PCA-24 fit reads train `reconstruction_r2`=0.07 but raw held-out EV 0.62, which is only possible across conventions. So please disregard the implied 'train→held-out gap' framing in the table; the real, convention-consistent finding is just: **the multi-atom manifold dictionary's raw held-out reconstruction is well below a trivial linear-PCA baseline and degrades with K.**

--- Comment 3/10 by @SauersML (2026-07-08T14:49:56Z) ---
Two of the three legs of this failure are now isolated with numbers (2026-07-08, manifold-zoo arena micro: K=6 atoms, 6 planted factors incl. circle/sphere/disk, L0=2, N=700):

1. **Terminal-state loss — FIXED** (`73dd39009`): the outer ρ search's probes repeatedly walk the shared warm-start state into the collapse basin; the per-call #1026 incumbent restores within a call, but the good basin decayed *across* calls (0.77 → 0.54 → 0.38). A fit-LEVEL reconstruction incumbent (banked at every accepted outer iterate under `prefer_candidate_basin`, consulted once at `into_fitted` entry) now returns the search's best-visited basin: **native train R² 0.7538** where the pre-fix terminal state reconstructed at 0.18.

2. **Held-out EV low — isolated to the cold OOS encode path**: `converged_latents` on the *same training rows* collapses 0.7538 → **0.2048** (test 0.2468 ≈ cold-train, so NOT a generalization gap), and warm-starting the OOS solve with the fit's own converged coords/logits is *worse* (0.0186) — dispositive that `sae_manifold_predict_oos` (frozen-decoder solve, PCA-self-seeded; `latent_basis_and_sae_ffi_tail.rs:648`) optimizes/decodes something different from the training reconstruction (scaling/gate/amplitude/hybrid-image divergence), or the `initial_coords` (K,N,D_max) marshalling contract is off. Repro discriminator prints are in `bench/bsf_manifold_zoo.py::_fit_ours_rust` (native vs cold vs warm).

--- Comment 4/10 by @SauersML (2026-07-08T14:53:19Z) ---
Root-cause mechanism identified and the structural fix landed. The evidence criterion RANKED COLLAPSE BETTER than structure: the barrier's collapse cost saturated at O(1) (−½·s·ln ε) while the Laplace collapse reward is extensive in the data — measured on real activations as basins hundreds of nats lower within Δρ≈1e-2 (the #2087 envelope probes). Fix: the occupancy-scaled Jeffreys barrier −½·Σ_C N_eff,C·log det(F_C + ε_C·I) (on main; penalties.rs) — collapse cost now grows with the co-fired data, in the same N_eff currency the rank charge prices dimensions, with ε_C = 2√(s/min N_eff) derived from the Wigner/MP bulk edge (constant removed). The evidence-ordering flip is pinned by a new test (occupancy_scaled_barrier_flips_collapse_evidence_ordering), and a barrier-engaged K≥2 FD gate guards value/gradient consistency.

Real-data validation (K2.5 layer-40, 20k rows): 9/9 configs completed with ZERO co-collapse aborts, including all four historical always-abort shapes (r² 0.974 / 0.956 / 0.707 / 0.670). Held-out-EV-decreasing-in-K on planted mixtures should be re-measured post-landing — the mechanism this issue describes is exactly the one the scaling removes.

--- Comment 6/10 by @SauersML (2026-07-08T21:04:59Z) ---
Periodic (circle) ARD math corrected in 7c95a0c31 — directly relevant to circle-atom evidence/precision here, though **not a claimed fix** for the co-collapse:

- **von-Mises normalizer** was missing the period Jacobian `n_eff·ln P` (`log Z = ln P − η + log I0(η)`, `η=α/κ²`). No-op at `P=1`; corrects non-unit periodic axes in absolute (cross-K/topology) evidence.
- **ARD empirical-Bayes precision** step was the Gaussian fixed point `α = φ̂·n_eff/(Σq + trH⁻¹)` — only the `η→∞` limit of the von-Mises criterion. Periodic axes now solve the exact stationary root `A(η) = 1 − 1/(2·η_gauss)`, `A=I1/I0`, `η_gauss=α_gauss/κ²`, by safeguarded bisection.

Worth re-measuring held-out EV vs K on the planted circle mixtures after this — the precision the outer loop assigns to circle axes was previously mis-scaled in the diffuse regime.


--- Comment 7/10 by @SauersML (2026-07-10T04:42:46Z) ---
## Remaining structural coupling found and fixed: the scale-gauge cure was never engaged on the public `sae_manifold_fit` path (missed-entry default) — flipped in 1f2981be8

Per the re-measure request, I traced the top-1 routing + gate/amplitude interaction on HEAD to check whether anything still couples atom supports after the landed fixes (fit-level incumbent 73dd39009, occupancy-scaled Jeffreys f46b1bccf, OOS-ρ* round-trip 71f06cce1, periodic-ARD 7c95a0c31). There was one live coupling left, and it is a plumbing gap, not new math:

**The mechanism (still live until today).** The default `ibp_map` gate is `a_k = σ(l_k/τ)·π_k` with the ordered stick-breaking mean `π_k = (α/(α+1))^{k+1}` (`assignment.rs::ibp_map_row`). Every atom's gate is capped by its column index — at α=1 that is 0.5, 0.25, 0.125, … — while the decoder smoothness penalty is scaled by λ only, so atom k's decoder is effectively over-shrunk by `1/π_k²` (4×, 16×, 64×…). On single-active planted mixtures with top-1 routing, each additional circle is served by a higher-index, harder-capped atom: exactly "held-out EV decreasing in K". Because all active atoms are over-shrunk in lockstep, the median-keyed collapse retraction never fires (no atom is small relative to its peers).

**The cure exists and is support-independent**: `pin_scale_gauge` (`fit_drivers.rs:5655-5676`) peels every atom's ‖B_k‖ into the UNPENALIZED log-amplitude `s_k` at accepted iterates (unit-B̂, scale-free smoothness) and re-homes `exp(s_k) ≈ 1/a_k` by a joint data-optimal solve with a monotone keep-best safeguard — so every active atom reaches the target regardless of its π_k cap, and healthy fits are inert. It is gated on `quotient_scale`.

**The gap**: d06c1255f flipped `quotient_scale` default→true on `sae_manifold_fit_inner`'s pyo3 signature (the precomputed-basis entry) and declared the public path engaged — but `gamfit.sae_manifold_fit` routes through `sae_manifold_fit_minimal` (`latent_basis_and_sae_ffi_tail.rs`), whose signature still said `quotient_scale = false`, and the Python facade never passes the kwarg. So every fit in this issue's repro family has run with the gauge OFF, including any post-d06c1255f re-measure. **Fixed in 1f2981be8**: the minimal entry now defaults true (the flag is forwarded verbatim into the shared inner: term switch + seed-decoder norm peel), matching the sibling entry and the term constructor (`construction.rs:211`).

**Why the landed set should now resolve this issue's headline numbers**, per leg:
- EV decreasing in K = π_k over-shrink, cured by the (now actually engaged) scale gauge; higher-index atoms keep unit-shape decoders with amplitude carrying the 1/π_k magnitude.
- Terminal-state decay across ρ probes = fit-level reconstruction incumbent (73dd39009) + objective-keyed incumbent (#2230, d10757054).
- Collapse ranked better than structure = occupancy-scaled Jeffreys barrier (f46b1bccf), extensive in co-fired N_eff.
- Train-vs-held-out gap = OOS solve now decodes under the fit's ρ* (71f06cce1).

**Confirming measurement** (one shot, wheel ≥ 1f2981be8): the issue's own planted-circle sweep — C=3/p=12 and C=6/p=24, K ∈ {C, C+2, 2C}, `top_k=1`, held-out `ev(test, reconstruct(test))`. Accept: EV non-decreasing in K and ≥ the matched-rank linear-PCA floor (0.73/0.55). A cheap in-tree discriminator already exists (`tests_collapse_2132`), but the sweep on the Python surface is the honest close-out since the defect was in the FFI default.


--- Comment 8/10 by @SauersML (2026-07-10T14:56:42Z) ---
## Acceptance-harness audit: the landed driver currently asks an impossible question

`experiments/scale_close/driver_2132_planted_circle_ev_vs_k.py` currently computes a fresh PCA baseline at `rank=K` and requires the curved fit to beat it by +0.05 for every K in the sweep.

That conflicts with this thread's latest requested sweep `K ∈ {C, C+2, 2C}`. The planted signal lives in exactly `2C` orthogonal linear directions, so at `K=2C` a rank-K PCA spans the entire noiseless signal. No curved model can beat that EV-optimal full-signal linear reconstruction by +0.05. The existing harness therefore cannot pass even for an oracle curved dictionary.

The thread's stated acceptance numbers — PCA floors 0.73 for C=3/p=12 and 0.55 for C=6/p=24 — are the fixed rank-C linear baselines from the original reproduction, not a rank-K baseline that grows through 2C.

I am correcting the close driver to the actual issue contract:

1. run C=3/p=12 and C=6/p=24 with K={C,C+2,2C}, top_k=1;
2. compute one fixed rank-C PCA floor on the identical held-out split;
3. require curved held-out EV at every K to clear that floor;
4. require curved EV to be non-decreasing in K (within the explicitly reported numerical tolerance).

This is a harness correction, not a relaxation: it restores the exact comparator and sweep named in the issue and removes a mathematically impossible +0.05-over-rank-2C condition.

Mechanism update from the criterion-completeness fix (`5df164b08`): the ranked REML value omitted the decoder repulsion and the Jeffreys separation barrier (plus ScadMcp/BlockOrthogonality) while the inner KKT gradient carried all of them — a documented 'residual inconsistency' that is inert at K=1 but live exactly in this issue's regime: K≥2 near-collinear decoders, where those terms hold energy. The ρ-search was therefore ranking a criterion whose envelope theorem was violated at every co-collapse-adjacent optimum — the anti-collapse terms shaped the Newton step but never shaped model selection. The criterion now prices the complete penalized objective (v's base = penalized_objective_total exactly), so the barrier/repulsion machinery finally participates in the outer ranking that decides between collapsed and separated basins. The structural fix for cold-joint K≥2 remains per-block confinement (#2023); this closes the scoring half. Worth re-running this issue's planted-mixture panel after CI greens.

ISSUE #2228: SAC stagewise/manifold fit: RemlConvergenceError (inner solve stalls at fixed ρ) at LLM width p=4096 and on clean synthetic circles
================================================================================
Author: SauersML
Created: 2026-07-08T01:49:53Z
URL: https://github.com/SauersML/gam/issues/2228
Comments: 14
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
BODY:
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
## Summary

`sae_manifold_fit_stagewise` (and `sae_manifold_fit`) raise `RemlConvergenceError` — "inner solve did not converge at fixed ρ; objective stalled for 3 consecutive refine rounds" with a large residual KKT gradient (`‖g‖ ≈ 1e1–1e2`) — on LLM-width residual-stream activations (p = 4096), under **both** the Euclidean and the behavioral-Fisher metrics, and it does not terminate within 5 min at p = 4096. The same failure reproduces on **clean low-dimensional synthetic circle data**, so it is not specific to the LLM acts.

This blocks the App-B "Fisher currency" A/B (iid vs GLS reconstruction) from using the stagewise engine; that experiment fell back to a closed-form rank-r linear reconstructor. Filing so the fitter is fixed for the manifold path. Likely the same wide-`p` / structural-coherence cluster as #2080 / #1094.

## Repro

gamfit 0.1.250 (wheel `gamfit-0.1.250-cp310-abi3-manylinux_2_28`).

### A. clean synthetic circle, p = 8, K = 1

```python
import numpy as np, gamfit
rng = np.random.RandomState(0)
n, p = 120, 8
th = rng.uniform(0, 2*np.pi, n)
X = np.zeros((n, p)); X[:,0] = np.cos(th); X[:,1] = np.sin(th)
X += 0.05*rng.randn(n, p)
gamfit.sae_manifold_fit(np.ascontiguousarray(X), K=1, d_atom=1,
    atom_topology="circle", assignment="ibp_map", fisher_factors=None,
    n_iter=30, random_state=0)
# -> GamError: SaeManifoldTerm::reml_criterion: inner solve did not converge at
#    fixed ρ; neither the KKT gradient ‖g‖=1.37e2 nor the quotient KKT gradient
#    ‖Π⊥gauge g‖=1.37e2 met tolerance 3.45e-4
```

### B. real Qwen residual-stream acts, p = 4096, stagewise

```python
import numpy as np, gamfit
X = ...  # (70, 4096) last-token residual acts, mean-centered
gamfit.sae_manifold_fit_stagewise(np.ascontiguousarray(X), d_atom=1,
    atom_topology="circle", assignment="ibp_map", structured_whitening=False,
    fisher_factors=None, max_births=8, max_backfit_sweeps=2, n_iter=40,
    random_state=0)
# -> RemlConvergenceError: inner solve did not converge at fixed ρ; objective
#    stalled for 3 consecutive refine rounds (‖g‖=1.27e1, tol 2.6e-4) and the
#    undamped evidence factorization failed at each stall point
#    [RESEED-DIAG collapse_events=0 dict_reseeds=0 struct_reseeds=0]
# structured_whitening=True fails identically; hangs >5 min before erroring.
```

Both metrics (`fisher_factors=None` and a behavioral-Fisher shard) fail the same way. At p = 4096 the fit also does not return within 5 min.

## Expected

The stagewise / manifold fit should converge (or return a best-incumbent with a soft-fail flag) on a well-conditioned single circle at small p, and on mean-centered LLM-width acts. The REML inner solve stalling at a large `‖g‖` far above tol, with the undamped evidence factorization failing at the stall point, suggests the inner Newton/quotient step is not making progress under rank-deficient geometry at LLM width — a hard error here makes the manifold path unusable for reconstruction A/Bs.

## Notes

- Seen while landing App-B (behavioral-Fisher "nats currency"): the closed-form rank-r GLS-vs-PCA reconstructor was used instead and returns cleanly, so the currency measurement is unblocked — but the manifold fitter itself is the bug.
- `RESEED-DIAG collapse_events=0` on the p=4096 case (no reseeds fired), while the p=8 synthetic shows structural-coherence collapse/reseed churn — consistent with the co-collapse cluster.

1. `zz_2087_third_order_envelope_discriminator_softmax` (tests/sae/sae/sae_outer_gradient_fd_gate.rs, landed `6255adc`) shows the inner landscape near these fits is **basin-discontinuous**: warm-started re-solves at ρ±h return the warm start exactly for small h, while a collapse basin with a criterion hundreds of units lower sits Δρ≈1e-2 away. Stall-then-refuse at a genuine ‖g‖ plateau is the honest local behavior of that geometry — the fix axis is the outer gradient/criterion consistency (see the #2080 comment), not more inner refinement budget.
