ISSUE #2260: Gradient circle-SAE readout is seed-unstable on larger-model activations (orderings 0.67-0.97 across seeds at EV~0.98)
================================================================================
Author: SauersML
Created: 2026-07-11T15:25:07Z
URL: https://github.com/SauersML/gam/issues/2260
Comments: 1
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
BODY:
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
**TL;DR:** On OLMo-2-7B activations, the gradient (torch-lane) circle fit is seed-unstable even when reconstruction is excellent: fitted calendar orderings span **0.67–0.97 across seeds 42–44** at the 609B-token checkpoint and **0.54–0.79** at the final checkpoint (3896B), at EV ≈ 0.98 — while the fit-free class-mean-plane readout on the same data sits at **0.98–0.99**. High EV does not certify a stable latent parameterization.

*AI-filed (Silico agent, run by Scott); numbers from recorded overnight-experiment artifacts.*

**Roadmap:** L3 in the five-experiment synthesis ledger (experiment #6).

## Mechanism

In the 7B's **6-dimensional** day-class subspace, a closed curve can reconstruct the cloud well while **wandering through the 4 dimensions outside the ordering plane** — which scrambles the latent angles run-to-run. The 1B subspace didn't leave the fit that freedom. So the failure is not "the fit didn't converge": it converged, to a high-EV curve whose latent coordinate is under-determined by the reconstruction objective.

## Measured consequences

- The multi-seed significance rule **never passes at 7B** — at any checkpoint — even where the plane ordering is 0.987. A user relying on the fitted angle would conclude the circle isn't there; the deterministic readout shows it plainly.
- On 1B the fit does converge to the plane readout late (seed orderings 0.966–0.971 at 4001B, multi-seed significant) but is noisy mid-training: an earlier onset bracket (21–210B tokens) turned out to be **partly fit noise** — the fit-free readout shows the ordering already complete at 21B.

## Proposed fixes

1. **Subspace-restricted fit:** an option to constrain (or penalize) the curve's out-of-plane components when a target subspace is known — e.g. restrict the decoder to the top-2 plane of class means, letting reconstruction spend the remaining dimensions but not the latent coordinate.
2. **Per-seed latent-angle agreement diagnostic:** report cross-seed circular concordance of the latent angles alongside EV, so users see instability instead of trusting EV.
3. **Docs:** state explicitly that EV alone does not validate the latent coordinate.

## Evidence (recorded artifacts, cluster paths)

- Per-seed orderings + EVs per checkpoint: `/mnt/data/shared/silico/experiments/exp_01kx840etdfy7v0k5z81sjdd2t/worktree/experiments/experiment-5/results/robustness.json`
- Fit-vs-plane comparison and multi-seed significance per checkpoint: same dir, `emergence_1b_vs_7b.json`, `plane_trajectory_7b.json`, `plane_trajectory_1b.json`
- Mid-training 1B seed ranges: experiment #4's Table 1 (results page in the same thread)


--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
COMMENTS (1):
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

--- Comment 1/1 by @SauersML (2026-07-11T18:28:11Z) ---
Disposition from the audit: this is a latent identifiability/reporting gap, not a convergence gap — a high-EV curve wanders the extra dimensions of the class subspace, scrambling t across seeds, and EV structurally cannot detect it (any chart of the same image scores identically). Two concrete fixes, both stage-5 follow-ups recorded on #2023: cross-seed coordinate concordance reported alongside EV (the direct measurement of this issue's 0.67–0.97 spread), and a subspace-confinement option so the chart is estimated inside a fixed r-dim subspace rather than free to rotate. The convergence-repair stack (#2228) is still relevant here: seed-instability measurements are only meaningful when each seed actually reaches its optimum, which the terminal Newton phase now enforces rather than budget-truncating at seed-dependent plateaus.

ISSUE #2261: Curved-arm training budget: default fits undertrain vs closed-form linear baselines; consider warm-starting from the linear/PCA solution
================================================================================
Author: SauersML
Created: 2026-07-11T15:25:08Z
URL: https://github.com/SauersML/gam/issues/2261
Comments: 1
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
BODY:
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
**TL;DR:** At the k-sweep default training budget (1500 steps), the torch `ManifoldSAE` trails the closed-form SVD top-K baseline at **every** K on real Qwen3-8B activations. At 4× the budget (6000 steps) it ties at K = 16 (held-out EV 0.99289 ± 0.00036 over 3 seeds vs 0.99284 for SVD) and is **still climbing** at K = 32 (gap 0.0033 → 0.0016; extrapolated parity ~25k–50k steps) — at ~800 s/fit vs **0.45 s** for SVD at the same K. Proposal: **warm-start curved atoms from the linear/PCA solution.**

*AI-filed (Silico agent, run by Scott); numbers from recorded overnight-experiment artifacts.*

**Roadmap:** not in the synthesis ledger's L1–L13 — an independent finding from experiment #2's convergence check, filed at researcher request.

## The asymmetry

Since a near-flat curved atom can approximate a linear direction locally, initializing curved atoms from the top-K PCA/SVD solution (decoder init + coordinate warm start) should start the fit at linear-parity and let curvature only improve from there — instead of spending tens of thousands of gradient steps recovering what the closed-form baseline gets for free in half a second.

## Measured numbers (K {16, 32} × steps {1500, 3000, 6000} × 3 seeds, N = 200k, shared PCA-64 chart)

| K | steps | held-out EV (mean ± sd) | SVD top-K | gap | s/fit |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|
| 16 | 1500 | 0.99054 ± 0.00045 | 0.99284 | 0.0023 | 199 |
| 16 | 6000 | 0.99289 ± 0.00036 | 0.99284 | −0.00006 (**closed**) | 802 |
| 32 | 1500 | 0.99531 ± 0.00016 | 0.99862 | 0.0033 | 496 |
| 32 | 6000 | 0.99701 ± 0.00020 | 0.99862 | 0.0016 (**still climbing**) | 1956 |

The deltas are well outside seed noise (pooled seed sd ≤ 0.0005). So "curved fits lose to linear baselines" at default budgets is an artifact of undertraining, not of the model class — but closing the gap by brute steps costs three orders of magnitude more compute than the baseline it's chasing.

## Suggested directions

1. Warm-start: decoder blocks initialized from the top-K SVD directions, coordinates from the projections (the existing `t_init`/`a_init` contract already accepts this).
2. Or expose/raise the default budget with a convergence-aware stop, so the k-sweep default doesn't silently compare an undertrained curved arm against a converged closed-form baseline.

## Evidence (recorded artifacts, cluster paths)

- `/mnt/data/artifacts/silico/experiments/_flat/exp_01kx7qwdseen68mc2jhqaqvsan/results/curved_convergence_check.json` (the full grid + per-K verdicts)
- `/mnt/data/artifacts/silico/experiments/_flat/exp_01kx7qwdseen68mc2jhqaqvsan/results/perf_frontier.json` (EV-vs-K frontier incl. `svd_topk` timings)


--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
COMMENTS (1):
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

--- Comment 1/1 by @SauersML (2026-07-11T18:28:10Z) ---
Two landed changes address the undertraining mechanism here directly: (1) the default fit's inner budget was being consumed by a linear-rate crawl (contraction ~0.998/iter) — the terminal exact-Newton phase (#2228, `7763e8478`) now ends that crawl superlinearly at the stall plateau, so the same nominal budget reaches an actually-converged decoder instead of a truncated one; (2) Tier-0 input standardization (`d67d341c0`) removes the κ≈1e8 conditioning that set that rate. Note the objective-gated decoder-LSQ/coordinate-reprojection polish already iterates to its penalized-objective fixed point at every joint fit — i.e. the 'warm-start from the linear/PCA solution' this issue asks for is effectively present as the closed-form block-sweep tail; what was missing was the superlinear joint phase between the MM walk and that polish. Worth re-measuring the curved-vs-closed-form gap on this issue's benchmarks once CI is green on the stack.

ISSUE #2262: Shape adjudication on SAE feature groups: detection-reach limit for masked rings + high false-circle floor on structureless data - needs built-in controls
================================================================================
Author: SauersML
Created: 2026-07-11T15:25:08Z
URL: https://github.com/SauersML/gam/issues/2262
Comments: 0
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
BODY:
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
**TL;DR:** An unsupervised topology census over SAE feature groups (overcomplete SAE → co-activation clustering → per-group 2-D PCA → `adjudicate_atom_shape`) has **two failure modes in opposite directions**, both measured: it cannot reach the low-relative-variance rings that real concept circles actually live in, and it manufactures ring verdicts from structureless data at double-digit rates. The census workflow needs **built-in matched controls** to be trustworthy. This is the "how to make the census honest" companion to the centroid-ordering test in PR #2257.

*AI-filed (Silico agent, run by Scott); numbers from recorded overnight-experiment artifacts.*

**Roadmap:** L7 + L8 in the five-experiment synthesis ledger (experiment #6) — the adjudicator blind-spot bucket.

## 1. Detection reach

The pipeline's own validated positive control recovers a dominant synthetic ring near-perfectly (adjudicator circle margin **+0.867**, angle recovery r = **0.997**, ordering mc_p = 0.0005) — but **loses a ring masked by a linear factor at ≥ ~1× its radius**: ordering p = 0.16 at 1× masking, and the verdict degrades to `mixture_k4` at 2×. Real concept circles (weekday/month, confirmed in the same model with ordering r = 0.96 via a label-seeded class-mean projection) live exactly in this low-relative-variance regime — so the standard unsupervised route cannot certify them **even when they exist**.

## 2. False-circle floor

On structureless controls run through the *identical* pipeline, the adjudicator returns circle verdicts at rates **above** real data: shuffle **7/31** and Gaussian **9/47** adjudicator-circles vs real **1/41** (healthy dictionaries, mean L0 53–189). The centroid-ordering second tier also fires on controls (**4/10** shuffle, **3/11** Gaussian vs **6/28** real). Fisher tests: real is statistically indistinguishable from control (tier-1 p = 0.62, tier-2 p = 0.72). Sparse non-negative codes + per-group 2-D PCA manufacture ring-like geometry from nothing.

## 3. A confound that suppresses

Dense dictionaries (mean L0 ≳ 2000) suppress circle verdicts entirely — **0/377** across all dense configs. So the verdict rate is also an artifact of dictionary health, in the opposite direction: a raw rate is uninterpretable without knowing the code sparsity it was measured at.

## Recommendations for the library

0. **The principled fix: add a composite "ring-of-clusters" candidate class to the shape race** — a k-cluster mixture whose centroids are *constrained* to lie on a circle (fit center, radius, and k angles). On discrete cyclic concepts — the common case: real concepts take finitely many values — this class should beat both the free mixture (fewer effective parameters, captures the cyclic order) and the plain circle (explains the clumpy density). It would have adjudicated the measured weekday data correctly: 7 tight clusters (per-label angular concentration R = 0.998) arranged on a closed calendar-ordered loop (ordering r = 0.963 vs permutation-null 95th pct 0.366), which the current race calls `mixture_k5`. The bolt-on centroid-ordering test (PR #2257) stays as the cheap immediate mitigation; the constrained candidate class is the fix that lets the race own the verdict.
1. **Ship matched structureless controls as a built-in option** of the census/adjudication workflow: per-dimension shuffle + covariance-matched Gaussian, pushed through the same clustering + PCA + adjudication path, so users get a per-run false-circle floor for free.
2. **Document the masked-ring detection limit** (~1× radius) and the **dictionary-health gate**: report mean L0 next to any verdict rate.
3. **Consider a variance-normalized or label-free subspace search** that can reach low-relative-variance rings. The class-mean-subspace projection that recovers the real circles requires labels; the gap is an unsupervised equivalent (e.g. project out dominant linear factors before adjudication, or search 2-D subspaces for ring-likeness rather than taking top-2 variance).

## Evidence (recorded artifacts, cluster paths)

- Census summary (all rates, Fisher tests, positive-control table): `/mnt/data/shared/silico/experiments/exp_01kx7qkwd2f0xayc0yncfz9qhp/worktree/experiments/experiment-1/results/census_summary.json`
- Per-run verdicts + tier-2 ordering: `/mnt/data/artifacts/silico/experiments/_flat/exp_01kx7qkwd2f0xayc0yncfz9qhp/census/` (`verdict_*.json`, `ordering_*.json`) and dense-run `verdict_*.json` one level up

COMMENTS: (none)

ISSUE #2263: Steering dosimetry calibration + structure_certificate unusable on real activations
================================================================================
Author: SauersML
Created: 2026-07-11T15:28:30Z
URL: https://github.com/SauersML/gam/issues/2263
Comments: 1
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
BODY:
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
**TL;DR:** On real Qwen3-8B activations (layer 20, weekday/month circles), the steering path works — but its **dose calibration is far off at defaults**, and the **e-value `structure_certificate` cannot run at all** because it requires a minted closed-form fit (see the solver issue #2258). Items 1–3 are calibration/UX improvements with measured numbers; item 4 is a dependency of the solver fix.

*AI-filed (Silico agent, run by Scott); numbers from recorded overnight-experiment artifacts.*

**Roadmap:** L11 in the five-experiment synthesis ledger (experiment #6); item 4 is the user-facing face of L6 (filed separately).

## 1. Default amplitude/dose scaling is far too small on real activations

`fit.steer` amplitude-1 plans produce ~0.02-nat realized doses that move nothing behaviorally. An alpha sweep to **16** was needed to reach behavioral effect: **85–89% calendar-move rate at the concept token** (weekday 89%, month 85%) vs **58–61% for the matched-norm in-chart control** (and ~16% for a matched-norm random ambient direction). A user following the documented recipe at default amplitude will conclude steering doesn't work.

## 2. Predicted-vs-realized KL goes nonlinear across layers

The endpoint output-Fisher dose meter tracks well at small doses in-layer (median realized/predicted ratio 1.16–1.35 at the final-token site) but is off by **22× at alpha = 1 down to 0.27× at alpha = 16** when the dose is set 16 layers before the readout. This blocked precise dose targeting: there was no reliable way to request "N nats at the output" from a mid-stack intervention. Closed-loop dosing (search alpha against realized KL) was the workaround; it could ship as the recommended cross-layer recipe.

## 3. Month steers overshoot the requested target

Month rotations move in the right direction but overshoot: requested advances of +1..+6 months realized a mode of **+8**. Same calibration root as (1)–(2), listed separately because it changes the sign of the UX problem (not "nothing happens" but "too much happens").

## 4. `structure_certificate` unusable on real activations (dependency)

The e-value structure certificate and `validity_radius` require a minted closed-form fit, and the closed-form engine never returns one on this data (#2258) — so no run in the study could produce a certificate. Not a separate bug: fixing #2258 (or letting the certificate machinery accept torch-lane fits) resolves this. Filed here so the linkage is on record: the steering path currently ships with its certification layer unreachable in exactly the setting people want to steer in.

## Evidence (recorded artifacts, cluster paths)

- Per-steer records (arm, k, alpha, outcome, realized KL): `/mnt/data/artifacts/silico/experiments/_flat/exp_01kx7r4wtte1b8w64efhcs99de/cyclic_qwen3_8b_l20/steer_*_records.jsonl`
- Output-Fisher factors used for the dose predictions: same dir, `steer_*_fisher.npz`
- Move-rate / coherence / KL summaries per arm and site: experiment #3's `results/steering_stats.json` (worktree)

Same unblock as #2249: structure_certificate/dosimetry on real activations was gated on real-activation fits actually certifying, which the #2228 wall made impossible (0/39 on #2258's panel). ISSUE #2266: Certification stack (structure certificate, validity_radius) is keyed to the closed-form path and vanishes with it
================================================================================
Author: SauersML
Created: 2026-07-11T15:50:54Z
URL: https://github.com/SauersML/gam/issues/2266
Comments: 1
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
BODY:
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
**TL;DR:** The certification stack — the e-value structure certificate and `validity_radius` — is keyed to the closed-form fit path, so when the closed-form engine cannot mint a fit (which on real LLM activations is currently always, see #2258), **certification vanishes with it**: no run in a five-experiment study could produce a certificate, on any model, at any checkpoint. The checkpoint-dynamics drift path additionally carries no anytime-valid stability certificate of its own.

*AI-filed (Silico agent, run by Scott); from recorded overnight-experiment findings.*

**Roadmap:** L6 in the five-experiment synthesis ledger (experiment #6, `engineering_ledger.json`). User-facing consequence recorded as item 4 of #2263; root cause tracked in #2258.

## Why this is its own issue

Even with #2258 fixed, the coupling is a design fragility: the library's *only* certification path depends on the one engine that cannot converge from a cold start (#2258). Two clarifications on what "torch lane" means here: `ManifoldSAE.fit()` is a wrapper around the same closed-form rust solve (it only adds encoder-predicted warm starts), so it inherits both the solver and its certificates when it converges; the *manual gradient training loop* over `ManifoldSAE` parameters is the genuinely separate optimizer — it produces usable fits on exactly the data where cold-start closed-form refuses, and those gradient-trained fits cannot be certified at all.

## Suggested fix

Let the certificate machinery accept torch-lane fits (the claim ledger doesn't inherently need closed-form solve internals), or provide a torch-lane equivalent. Secondarily: an anytime-valid stability certificate for the checkpoint-dynamics drift path.

## Evidence

- Experiment #3's instrument note (certificate blocked; adjudicator + permutation null carried the shape claim instead): `/mnt/data/shared/silico/experiments/exp_01kx7r4wtte1b8w64efhcs99de/worktree/experiments/experiment-3/results/results.json` (`recovery_weekday.certificate`)
- Experiment #4's engine-limitation section (14/14 closed-form attempts failed certification on OLMo-2-1B)


--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
COMMENTS (1):
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

--- Comment 1/1 by @SauersML (2026-07-11T18:27:05Z) ---
Supporting data point for this issue's design position (certification should attach to the model state, not the closed-form path): the audit found the inner acceptance gate is effectively held hostage by the outer analytic gradient's exactness assumption — the ½λ² decrement is computed and logged but barred from accepting solely so the envelope-theorem ρ-gradient stays exact, which converted 'inner solve is slow' into 'no fit can be minted'. The landed repair keeps the strict contract but makes it reachable (terminal exact-Newton at the stall plateau, `7763e8478`), and the EFS routing flip (`072c01c57`) means the default outer search no longer consumes that gradient at all for small fits — the certificate machinery (EFS fixed-point + one final exact-gradient KKT certificate) is now the natural 'any lane that reaches a certified stationary state' shape this issue asks for. Remaining gap to fully realize it: the freeze-lane exception (inner_max_iter == 0 assembles an analytic gradient at a non-KKT state by contract) and attaching certification to `into_fitted` rather than the entry path.

COMMENTS (1):
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

--- Comment 1/1 by @SauersML (2026-07-11T18:26:49Z) ---
Cost anatomy for the 900-s example, from the full static audit: the wall time is multiplicative through the default pipeline — topology race (≤6 candidate REML fits/atom) × 2 structured-whitening passes (each installs a NEW likelihood and re-runs the entire outer ρ search) × outer iterations × line-search probes (each a full inner re-convergence to the same KKT gate) × refine rounds (16–64×) × up to ~1e3 inner iterations at contraction ~0.998. Hardware was never the binding constraint (this is why #1017 kept finding an idle GPU); the exponent was. The landed stack shrinks the two innermost factors — the terminal Newton phase ends the ~1e3-iteration crawl in O(10) steps (#2228, `7763e8478`) and EFS routing (`072c01c57`) removes the per-probe full re-convergence lane for small fits (EFS has no line search) — and Tier-0 standardization (`d67d341c0`) cuts the κ that sets the crawl rate. The remaining structural factor (race × whitening passes × structure search as a bundled default) is the stage-5 unbundling follow-up: seed → single certified fit as the default entry, with race/whitening/births as explicit composable stages.


================================================================================
ISSUE #2269: Outer-REML certification: gradient-only / matrix-free-TR path can't certify a flat-direction stationary optimum (no curvature or probe-noise rescue)
================================================================================
Author: SauersML
Created: 2026-07-11T16:01:48Z
URL: https://github.com/SauersML/gam/issues/2269
Comments: 1
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
BODY:
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
### Summary
#2253 fixed outer-REML certification for the common cases — interior, railed/λ→0, and flat-valley optima **when an analytic Hessian is available**. A residual gap remains: a fit that terminates on the **gradient-only / matrix-free-TR path** at a genuinely-stationary point whose residual lies along a *flat* direction has **no rescue** and fails to certify, even though no feasible step reduces the objective beyond tolerance.

### Mechanism
`certify_outer_optimality` (`crates/gam-solve/src/rho_optimizer/run.rs`) widens the stationarity bound for a projected gradient sitting modestly above the tight `solver_bound` via two rescues, and this path has access to **neither**:

1. **Curvature-scaled Newton decrement** `½·gᵀH⁻¹g ≤ objective_tol` (run.rs ~1642) — requires an **analytic Hessian** (`DeclaredHessianForm::Dense/Either`). Objectives with `Hessian::Unavailable` / operator-only can't use it.
2. **Measured probe-noise floor** `σ̂/Δ` (`result.flat_noise_grad_bound`, from #2241) — only computed by the `CostStallGuard` on the **ARC-bridge** path, **not** the opt-native matrix-free-TR path, which emits `CostStallFloor→CostStallFlatValley` with `flat_noise_grad_bound = None`.

So a genuinely-flat-direction optimum on the TR path (large Newton decrement, or no analytic Hessian at all) clears neither band and is rejected.

### Root cause
The absolute stationarity floor `abs = objective_scale·1e-9` (`outer_gradient_tolerance`, run.rs ~2377) is **tighter than the achievable round-off floor** of a matrix-factorization REML gradient (~`√ε·scale ≈ 1.5e-8·scale`). The curvature and probe-noise certificates work *around* this too-tight floor; the gradient-only path has no workaround.

### Fix directions (principled — pick one)
- **(a)** Compute the `σ̂/Δ` probe-noise floor on the opt-native TR path by exposing its trajectory scatter. NB: the naive `objtol/trust_radius` substitute is **unsafe** (a collapsed trust radius over-certifies), so this needs the real scatter, not a proxy.
- **(b)** Make the abs floor **round-off-aware**: `abs = max(objective_scale·1e-9, c·√ε·objective_scale)` so it never demands sub-round-off gradient precision on any path.
- **(c)** Operator-Hessian Newton decrement — estimate `gᵀH⁻¹g` via a few matrix-free operator applies (Lanczos/CG), extending rescue #1 to the TR path.

### Priority
Low/medium — the common cases certify post-#2253 (verified: pyffi `shared_tangent` + `gam-solve` curvature guards green). This is the honest residual, not a live blocker.


--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
COMMENTS (1):
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

--- Comment 1/1 by @SauersML (2026-07-11T18:25:46Z) ---
Landed `072c01c57`: `SMALL_OUTER_BFGS_MAX_PARAMS` 8 → 0, so every fixed-point-capable, penalty-like objective routes to EFS (ψ-carrying ones to HybridEfs) at **every** dimension. The ≤8-coordinate 'performance' crossover was sending exactly the failing SAE repros (2–7 ρ coordinates) into the Strong-Wolfe/probe lane — the consumer of the entire wall/escape/rescue apparatus, where every cost probe is a full inner re-convergence — while large fits already ran the robust trace-based fixed point that needs no line search and no value/gradient-lane agreement. BFGS remains the fallback for objectives with no fixed-point hook or after `disable_fixed_point`. Plan tests inverted accordingly (`plan_efs_selected_few_params_when_penalty_like`, `plan_hybrid_efs_selected_few_params`).

This also moots the largest chunk of this issue's rescue-asymmetry concern for SAE: the certificate rescues exist to serve BFGS exits, and SAE small fits no longer take that lane except as fallback.


================================================================================
ISSUE #2271: Fitted ManifoldSAE cannot be round-tripped: save/load drops the fitted decoder curve and the uncertainty band
================================================================================
Author: SauersML
Created: 2026-07-11T16:19:54Z
URL: https://github.com/SauersML/gam/issues/2271
Comments: 1
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
BODY:
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
**TL;DR:** A fitted `ManifoldSAE` cannot be persisted as a first-class artifact: `save`/`load` (and `to_dict`/`from_dict`) drop the fitted state needed to re-render or reuse the manifold — the docs already note that `shape_uncertainty` raises after a round-trip (the Laplace covariance and band are dropped), and in practice a full experiment's saved artifacts end up containing raw activations and per-point coordinates but **not the fitted decoder curve**. Every downstream plot or reuse must recompute the fit.

*AI-filed (Silico agent, run by Scott); grounded in this thread's recorded artifacts.*

**Roadmap:** not in the synthesis ledger's L1–L13 — caught in post-run artifact review.

## Concrete case (measured artifact inventory)

An overnight recover→certify→steer study on Qwen3-8B weekday/month circles saved everything it could:

- `recovery_weekday.npz` / `recovery_month.npz`: raw activations (84×4096 per layer, L18–22), `labels`, `template_ids`
- `recovery_*_coords.json`: per-point angles and 2-D coordinates
- `steer_*_fisher.npz`: output-Fisher factors `U` (84×4096×8), `mass_residual`, prompts

None of these contain the fitted atom decoder — so the fitted closed curve (**the actual manifold**) cannot be re-rendered or re-used after the run without refitting from scratch. The instability in #2260 makes that worse: a refit is not guaranteed to reproduce the same latent parameterization, so "refit to re-plot" can silently change the object being plotted.

## The two facets are one serialization gap

1. `save`/`load` and `to_dict`/`from_dict` drop the posterior decoder covariance, so `shape_uncertainty` raises `ValueError` on a reloaded model (currently documented as a known limitation in `docs/manifold-sae.md`).
2. There is no supported way to persist and reload the fitted decoder curve + coordinates + topology as a renderable object; users fall back to saving raw inputs and refitting.

## Proposed fix

Make serialization round-trip the full fitted state: decoder coefficients per atom, per-atom per-token coordinates, resolved topology, and the decoder covariance / uncertainty band (or enough of the Laplace factor to reconstruct it) — so a fitted `ManifoldSAE` can be reloaded and its curve + band re-rendered without refitting. If the joint covariance is too large to persist by default, an opt-in (`save(..., with_uncertainty=True)`) beats the current silent drop.

## Evidence (recorded artifacts, cluster paths)

- `/mnt/data/artifacts/silico/experiments/_flat/exp_01kx7r4wtte1b8w64efhcs99de/cyclic_qwen3_8b_l20/` — `recovery_weekday.npz`, `recovery_month.npz`, `recovery_*_coords.json`, `steer_*_fisher.npz` (the complete inventory above; no fitted decoder present)
- `docs/manifold-sae.md`, the "uncertainty arrays are populated only on a freshly-fit model" note


--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
COMMENTS (1):
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

--- Comment 1/1 by @SauersML (2026-07-11T18:28:50Z) ---
Persistence surface note: the fitted artifact now carries one more field — `tier0_scale` (per-column σ from the new Tier-0 input standardization, `d67d341c0`) exported by the FFI beside `tier0_mean`. Any save/load path fixed under this issue must round-trip it: a consumer reconstructing from the per-atom `decoder_B` decodes in the standardized frame and must lift `μ + σ ⊙ x̂` (the in-tree `add_tier0_mean_inplace` does this; `None` σ = historical unstandardized path, including all behavior/crosscoder fits). Dropping σ on load would silently mis-scale every reconstruction by up to the per-column RMS ratio, which on raw activation targets is ~1e4 — worth an explicit round-trip assertion in this issue's test.
